A higher mammal or other Stage 4 system without Stage 5 has V as a purely individual variable: what constitutes "persisting" and "disintegrating" for it is determined by its own existence in the environment. This form of V, which is the initial form for stage 4, is hereafter referred to as individual V. At stage 5, this single-level structure of V is extended through a bidirectional M↔Y loop with physically retained traces; this extension is elaborated in section 3.5.

**V as a calibration of temporality.** From the variability of V follows a substantive observation that is important for linking stage 4 with section 5 (time as an emergent quantity). Since V determines what is considered a disintegration for the system, it thereby determines which changes are significant for the system - those that bring disintegration closer or push it further away are significant. And significance determines what the system retains as the past (recorded significant changes) and what it models as the future (predicted significant changes). The structure of the past and the future is the structure of the system's own time. V does not generate time - time as a mechanism is the same for all systems; it is a property of correlations between subsystems (Section 5). But V calibrates the system's temporality, defining the structure and horizon of its own time.

**What is cut off.** A proto-agent system without a class of agentic causal nodes in its models, or without imposing its own configuration onto this class, remains at stage 3 regardless of how complex the environment model may be. A chess program performs highly complex operations, has a model of the "board" and a model of "itself as a player," but its models lack a class of agentic causal nodes with the boundary states of retention/disintegration: its environment is the position of the pieces on the board; there are no configurations within it that retain or disintegrate as agent nodes. Therefore, a latent invariant does not emerge, self-overlay is impossible, and the program remains at stage 3 - regardless of computational power.

The structural status of existing large neural networks, including language models in their current architecture, remains open within the framework of the theory. A class of agentic causal nodes emerges in their models, but determining whether self-overlay of the latent invariant is realized in their operation in a strict structural sense requires an operational program, which is developed in Section 10.3. Until its results are available, the theory does not assign a specific rung on the ladder to existing information-causal architectures.

**What is covered.** Empirically - Homo sapiens in their full form. Apparently, higher mammals to one degree or another; possibly some birds (corvids) and cephalopods. The boundary here is empirically fuzzy, because structural conditions are difficult to measure in an external system. This is an open empirical problem to which the theory verification program (Section 10) pertains.

**A new type of gradient.** Transition 3 introduces a new type of gradient: an ontological one, between two possible states of the system itself as a whole - between "holding together" and "falling apart." This is no longer a spatial gradient in the environment (as in stage 0), nor a gradient between alternative states of the system at a given flow (stage 1), nor a structural gradient between architectures (stage 2), nor a temporal gradient between rates (stage 3). This is a gradient within the very ontological space of the system's states - between its existence and non-existence in the specific sense defined by V for systems of this type. Structurally, this gradient is induced by the retention contour over the continuous physics of Y through the boundary states of causal nodes: the difference "held together / falling apart," which exists objectively in Y, is transferred to the system through the self-overlay of a latent invariant. Against the backdrop of the sequence of gradient types accumulating through the ladder, this is the most fundamental of those that have emerged: for the first time, the gradient operates not between something and something within the system or around the system, but between two possibilities of the system itself as a whole.

**The retention mechanism at stage 4: preventive planning.** At stages 1, 2, and 3, the system's retention was reactive or active, but not conscious. At stage 1 - passive hysteresis. At stage 2 - causal self-sufficiency of a closed loop. At stage 3 - active alignment of the environment with the model of the current gradient. At stage 4, a new level emerges: preventive action based on a model of a possible future that includes the system's own possible non-existence. A bacterium moves toward glucose when there is already little of it left. A person stocks up on food for the winter when summer is in full swing. These are different horizons of retention, and the transition between them is possible only because V appears in the model as a pole relative to which actions can be projected into the distant future.

**The presence of inherited gradients in V constitutes the structural consolidation of the phenomenon.** Here we approach the fact that this theory contains a substantive operationalization of the identity of structure and phenomenon, elaborated in Section 6. In stages 1-3, the disruption of gradients occurs within the system: the system disintegrates, depletes itself, loses its ability to act, but these disruptions remain external events for it - the system has no vantage point from which they would become something for it. The Benard cell has no such vantage point relative to the falling flow. A bacterium does not have such a position relative to the toxin in the environment; its signaling networks respond to molecules, but this response has no inner aspect.

At stage 4, the situation changes fundamentally. The emergence of V as a structural pole means that, for the first time, a position arises from within the system, and disruptions to inherited gradients begin to be present in V - becoming, for the system, something relative to its own maintenance. This is not a functional act of fixing the superstructure (such as a device registering a signal); it is an ontological mode in which the structure becomes present to itself through V.

Hunger is the presence of a weakening of the energy gradient (inherited from stage 0) in V. Pain is the presence of a threat to the integrity of form (inherited from stage 1) in V. Anxiety is the presence of instability in causal closure (stage 2) or disruptions in modeling (stage 3) in V. Fear is the direct presence of a threat to V - the approach of the "I am disintegrating" state. These states - the phenomenal content of stage 4 - are not an arbitrary set of feelings that must be explained separately by neuroscience. They are structurally necessary modes of presence in which disruptions of each of the inherited gradients acquire experiential content through the V pole.

This provides the theory with an operational link to the philosophical thesis regarding the identity of structure and phenomenon (Section 6). Phenomenal experience does not arise on top of structure as a mysterious additional layer. It is the way in which structure is present to itself from within its own position through V. Without stage 4, there is no such position; without a position, there is no presence; without presence, there is no phenomenal content. The structural position and the experienced content are ontologically identical, because the experienced is the inner side of what is structurally presence through V.

**The probabilistic nature of the transition.** The structural conditions for the transition from 3 to 4 are necessary. Their simultaneous fulfillment in a proto-agent system requires: sufficient complexity of the substrate to accumulate a class of agentic causal nodes; an environment containing such nodes, physically manifested through sensory channels; situations in which the system's own configuration falls into a region isomorphic to the boundary states of this class; a functional mechanism for globalizing the emerging node S across all activity. All conditions are probabilistically sufficient. In evolution, the transition 3→4 occurred significantly less frequently than the transition 2→3: the overwhelming majority of proto-agent lifelines did not develop consciousness. This is consistent with empirical evidence and is formally discussed in Section 3.6.

**Distinguishing between two levels of probability.** The probabilistic nature of the 3→4 transition applies to the situation **prior to** the structural event of self-overlay: even in a system with a suitable substrate and in a suitable environment, self-overlay may not occur for evolutionary, architectural, or environmental reasons, and the transition will not take place. This is the level of historical probability, discussed in full in Section 3.6. At this level, the absence of a transition in a specific system or lineage of systems is not a refutation of the theory - it is a normal outcome, consistent with its probabilistic nature.

Once self-overlay has actually occurred - node S has formed, variable V functions as a global pole, and GWT-accessibility ensures its globalization - the theory is no longer probabilistic but makes a deterministic claim: such a system possesses phenomenal experience. This follows from the thesis on the identity of structure and phenomenon (Thesis 6 of Section 1.1; justification - Section 6.3): phenomenal experience is ontologically identical to the dynamics of self-modeling with pole V, and in the presence of this dynamic, phenomenal experience exists by identity, not by probability.

**Prohibitive predicate.** A direct prohibitive statement follows from this identity. The theory prohibits the existence of a system with a structurally realized self-overlay of a latent invariant of an agentic causal node onto its own configuration, with a functioning binary pole V and its globalization - and yet without phenomenal experience. The construction "fulfilled self-overlay without phenomenality" is structurally impossible, because it implies simultaneously attributing to the system the presence of V and the absence of what V structurally entails (Section 6.4, detailed critique of the zombie argument). The empirical discovery of even a single such system would be a direct refutation of the theory, not a quantitative refinement of it. The operational form of this forbidden predicate is elaborated in subsection 10.2.

**On the operational program.** Establishing that self-overlay has occurred in a specific system does not boil down to measuring a single parameter. A structural event manifests itself through a coupling of independent indicators, among which Φ is above the threshold value for causal integration, the presence of a self-representation node in the active inference formalism, GWT-accessibility of this node, prolonged hysteresis of altered behavior following the activation of pole V, expansion of behavioral sensitivity to aspects of Y not accessible at stage 3, and deviation of behavior from the prediction of the proto-agent's null model. Each indicator has an independent methodological basis; their joint coupling when creating the conditions for V activation is a necessary and sufficient operational condition for registering the transition. The threshold values of the indicators are not known a priori and are established empirically during the theory verification program by comparing systems that do or do not demonstrate the characteristic features of stage 4 in behavior. A full elaboration of this approach and its implementation across three lines of verification (biological, artificial, and synthetic biology) is provided in subsection 10.2.

**Macro-models of the transition.** Here they are weaker than for transitions 1 and 2. Conceptual - the difference between a chess program and a soldier in a trench (identical computational complexity, different model structure). Physical - it is absent in the form of a system on which the transition can be directly observed at the moment it occurs. This is the central open experimental problem of modern science of consciousness. Computational - partial models of self-representation in neural networks (self-other distinction, model-based reinforcement learning with a self-model), which have not yet achieved the realized self-overlay of a latent invariant.

**The absence of a robust physical macro-model** is not a flaw in the formalization, but rather an indication of an open experimental direction. Its direct formulation is the theory's second prediction (Section 10.2): to construct an artificial system satisfying the structural conditions of self-overlay, and subject it to an activating signal, observing whether a qualitative shift in behavior with phase-transition characteristics occurs. A fundamental caveat regarding such an experiment: V in the artificial system will have a content specific to its type. For information-causal systems, V is structurally realized as a pole between the coherence and the breakdown of the information-causal structure (Section 10.3). Therefore, one should not expect anthropomorphic fear or panic, but rather a qualitative shift in behavior calibrated by the type of V in this system.

The formal definition of stage 4 describes the structural event of the self-overlay of a latent invariant and, through the mechanism of the presence of inherited gradients in V, largely operationalizes the phenomenal nature of stage 4. A full elaboration of the philosophical aspect of the question - why presence through V is an experience from within, rather than merely a functional event - is provided in Section 6, particularly 6.3.

## 3.5. Transition 4: Model Recursion and the Environment Filter

The transition from stage 4 to stage 5 occurs when **a bidirectional M↔Y loop** is established in the population of stage 4 systems **via physically retained traces**: models of one configuration produce physical traces in Y; these traces are stably preserved in Y as states of Y, enter the simulation of other configurations through their own sensory channels, reconfigure their V-models, and the reconfigured models produce new traces. This transition is **a probabilistic event**: among a population of stage 4 systems with physically retained traces in Y, it **is possible** but not inevitable. On Earth, essentially only one species has undergone it in its complete form; several others have emerged in partial forms.

**Structural sequence.** First, an individual V (stage 4) is formed - through the self-overlay of the latent invariant of the agentic causal node onto the system's own configuration (section 3.4). If there are physically retained traces of V-carriers' behavior in the Y environment, the transition to stage 5 becomes **possible**: the traces can enter the modeling of other carriers and, under certain conditions, reconstruct their V-models. The realization of this possibility is a separate probabilistic event requiring the coincidence of the additional conditions listed below.

**Minimum condition.** (0) There exists a population of carriers with a self-overlayd latent invariant - configurations satisfying the conditions of stage 4 (Section 3.4). This is a background condition: stage 5 builds upon stage 4. The further conditions (a)-(d) are specific to stage 5. (a) The activity of carriers leaves physically persistent traces in the environment Y - stable changes in the states of Y that exist on timescales exceeding the lifetime of a single carrier. (b) The structure of interaction between carriers is such that traces regularly enter the modeling of other carriers through their sensory channels. (c) Upon entering the modeling, traces **reconfigure the V-model** of the perceiving configuration - not only channeling its behavior but also altering the retention/decay structure within its own model. (d) The restructured V-model produces new traces that enter the modeling of subsequent configurations.

Recursion is triggered when steps (a) through (d) are performed. Formally: let M*n denote the aggregate model of the population in generation n. Then \*\*M*{n+1} = F(M*n, E_n, R_n)\*\*, where E_n is the state of the environment (physical facts), R_n is the output of the previous recursion (physically retained traces of models from previous carriers), and F is the operator for integration and the generation of new models. Crucially, R_n enters the environment for the next generation and simultaneously serves as the material for constructing M*{n+1}. This is the recursive loop M₁ → Y → M₂ → Y → M₃: the product of the previous simulation cycle becomes both the environment and the material for the next cycle.

**The criterion for stage 5 is the restructuring of the V-model, not the channeling of behavior.** This structural distinction defines the boundary of stage 5. A physical trace can operate in two modes. In the first mode, the trace **channels the behavior** of another configuration: it changes its trajectory of motion, the thermodynamic costs of possible actions, and local stability probabilities, without entering its V-model. This is the mode of stigmergy in the broad sense - the configuration interacts with the altered environment through its reactions, without restructuring the retention/disintegration framework within its own model. This is **a precursor to the circuit**, not Stage 5. In the second mode, the trace **reconfigures the V-model** of another configuration: it enters its model as a structural element that alters the probability distribution of retention/disintegration in its offline simulation. **Only the second mode is stage 5**. The distinction can be empirically verified by analyzing whether the trace alters the operation of the V-model of the subsequent configuration, or only its immediate reactions to the environment.

Restructuring the V-model through the trace **does not require** the configuration to be able to interpret the trace as a sign. The trace functions as a physical constraint in Y: a sustained change in the state of the environment that narrows the space of possible configurations for those who operate within this environment through their models. The compatibility of the trace and the new configuration is ensured by the general physics of Y, not by interpretation.

**The role of Y as a structural filter of the loop.** The recursion M*n → M*{n+1} is not autonomous. The environment E_n acts upon it in a deferred selection mode: models that diverge too greatly from the structure of Y's causal constraints do not become established - not frame by frame, not every single one, not for every agent, but on average and over the long term. This does not make the recursion a deterministic environment; it keeps it consolidated to physical reality through a slow, nonlinear, yet real pressure. Pure fantasy without an consolidate in facts will collapse over time - not in every single case, but as a general statistical pattern.

It is precisely this structure that distinguishes Level 5 from two conceivable but empirically unworkable alternatives. Direct realism ("the environment dictates the model") is incorrect: the model generates the next model largely autonomously through recursion. Radical constructivism ("the model generates itself from itself") is incorrect: models that do not stand up to reality testing do not become established. Stage 5 is the strict middle ground: model recursion filtered by the environment through a bidirectional M↔Y loop.

**The type of the new gradient is - for the first time - beyond the boundaries of a single system.** Transition 4 introduces a new type of gradient: between historical states of a supra-individual structure. The sixth gradient exists between two states of the aggregate population model - M*n (the model of generation n) and M*{n+1} (the model of the next generation, enriched through the recursion F(M_n, E_n, R_n)). This is not a difference between two individual models, but between two states of the accumulated population model as a whole, and it manifests as a difference in informational content localized in the external material structures of individual carriers.

This is a qualitative shift that distinguishes stage 5 from all previous stages as a class, not merely as another level. At stages 1-4, every gradient constitutive of the stage could be localized within the system as such. At stage 5, the sixth gradient is localized for the first time outside a single system - it operates between states of a structure that transcends a single carrier. The complete sequence of gradient types and the logic of their accumulation, including this shift, are summarized in subsection 3.7.

**Expansion of the access spectrum to Y.** With the emergence of the bidirectional M↔Y loop via physical traces, Y becomes a two-layer system. To the physical layer inherited from stage 4 (Y as a structure of causal constraints in which the system maintains its position via V), a second layer is added - the space of physically retained traces of models from previous carriers. This is not an "information medium" in the sense of a non-physical abstraction; these are physical structures in Y with a thermodynamic realization according to Landauer. A fundamental feature of this aspect of Y is that it is accessible to the system not through its individual architecture, but through its inclusion in a population with a functioning M↔Y circuit. The stage 4 carrier has the structural prerequisites for accessing this layer (self-overlay of the latent invariant, V, globalization), but without participation in the circuit, this aspect is closed to it.

**The splitting of consolidation into two tempos.** The emergence of stage 5 fits into the logic of consolidation outlined in sections 3.3 and 3.4, but with one structural shift that distinguishes the 4→5 transition from all previous ones. At stages 1→4, consolidation operated at a single tempo - the tempo of the physical existence and reproduction of the individual carrier. At stage 5, consolidation **splits into two tempos** simultaneously. The first tempo is biological in the general sense: the tempo of reproduction of the individual carrier of stage 4, inherited from stage 4 without change. The second tempo is trace-based: the tempo of retaining physical traces in Y, exceeding the lifespan of the individual carrier. These two tempos are not reducible to one another. The splitting of rates is a structural condition for the very possibility of the sixth gradient - without it, the M↔Y circuit would operate at only one rate and would inevitably be reduced to an individual cycle.

This splitting directly implies the two-level structure of V at stage 5. The biological layer of V is maintained at the tempo of the individual carrier - it functions as a " " pole of the individual carrier's existence in Y. The trace layer of V is maintained at the tempo of physical traces in Y - it functions as a pole of the carrier's position in the accumulated population model. The two-level V is not an arbitrary expansion of V from one level to two; it is a structural consequence of the splitting of consolidation into two paces.

The splitting of consolidation into two rates at stage 4→5 is the final structural complication of the ladder.

**Distributed activity as a consequence of the distributed circuit.** From the localization of the sixth gradient outside a single system, it follows that activity at stage 5 becomes distributed for the first time. At stage 3, activity became possible through the temporal gradient; at stage 4, it acquired directionality through V. At stage 5, it ceases to belong to a single configuration - it functions as the coordinated action of a set of carriers through the common circuit M↔Y. Each carrier of stage 5 participates in the sixth gradient by receiving accumulated traces and generating new ones, but the gradient itself is not localized in any single carrier.

**The two-level structure of V and its three states.** The two-level nature of V implies the possibility of three qualitatively different states of its trace layer, which cannot be reduced to differences in the biological layer: **activated** (accumulated models are dense, the circuit operates at high voltage, the trace layer of V finds acute content in narratives - significance, threats, goals); **thinned-out** (the framework of the accumulated model has thinned, the circuit transmits models, but the density of their content is low - experienced as an existential vacuum); **balanced** (the framework of the accumulated model is dense, but the tension within it has faded - content exists but is not present as a living state, a condition historically preceding the drive toward catastrophic annihilation). These three states are independently described by different traditions: Frankl's clinical logotherapy (1963, 1969) with regard to the rarefied state, late Freud's psychoanalysis (1920, 1930), and cultural history (Stern, 1961; Schorske, 1979) as applied to the aligned state. The convergence of these three independent traditions in describing the same structural process from different angles is significant; the present theory provides a unified structural description of what the three traditions described using partial means.

One structural observation follows from the existence of the three states of the trace layer V. Stage 5 is not static - it unfolds over time with oscillations between these states: epochs of activated V are succeeded by epochs of rarefied or leveled V, and the transitions between them partially explain the observed cyclical nature of historical processes. Every historical cycle of culture is a micro-realization of the staircase pattern on the scale of several generations: accumulation of the content of the sixth gradient → retention of it as a dense framework → attainment of the aligned state → transition through catastrophe or renewal to a new cycle. This is consistent with the structural self-similarity of the pattern, discussed in Section 3.7.

**The author's thesis as a result of formalization**. It follows directly from conditions (a)-(d), from the recursive structure M\_{n+1} = F(M_n, E_n, R_n), and from the distributed nature of activity at stage 5 that, after transitioning to stage 5, consciousness becomes an active mechanism of complexity. This is not a separate statement added to the ladder; it is the direct content of the formal definition of stage 5. The conscious system of stage 5 does not passively exist in the environment - through the M↔Y loop, it generates physical structures that transform both the environment and the system itself through epigenetic and cultural pressure. The cycle of complexity closes: energy gradient → dissipative structure → autopoiesis → active inference → self-overlay of a latent invariant with pole V → bidirectional M↔Y loop → new structures in the environment and in the carriers themselves → accelerated complexity.

**Distinguishing between two classes of participants in stage 5.** Since stage 5 is tied to the structure of the M↔Y loop rather than to a biological substrate, a structural distinction follows that must be explicitly introduced.

**A conscious system of stage 5** is a configuration in which the conditions of stage 4 are fulfilled (self-overlay of a latent invariant, V as a structural pole, GWT accessibility) and which participates in the sixth gradient via the M↔Y circuit. In such a system, V is two-level: a biological layer plus a trace layer. This is a substantively conscious carrier of stage 5, possessing phenomenal experience with all its modes specific to this stage. Empirically, this class is represented on Earth by Homo sapiens, and by no one else in its full form.

**A participant in the contour structure** is a configuration or artifact that ensures the reception, integration, enrichment, or generation of traces in Y, without the need to fulfill the conditions of stage 4. This class includes, first and foremost, the Level 5 conscious systems themselves (since humans are both conscious systems and participants in the loop in one and the same person), but also material carriers of traces (texts, images, archives, digital repositories) and social structures (institutions of transmission, schools, libraries).

These two classes overlap at stage 5 conscious systems, but do not coincide. A stage 5 conscious system without participation in the loop is, for example, the last speaker of a dying language who has no conversation partners: its V is two-level in structure, but the loop no longer functions through it. A participant in the loop structure without a Level 5 conscious system is, for example, a text in an archive: it participates in the sixth gradient through preservation in Y, but has neither the conditions of Level 4 nor phenomenal experience.

**The boundary between model recursion and consciousness.** In this formulation, the boundary is clearly defined. Model recursion is the structural process M\_{n+1} = F(M_n, E_n, R_n), realized in the population and its material products. This process is the content of the sixth gradient and does not require that every participant in it meet the conditions of stage 4: it requires only that conditions (0) and (a)-(d) be satisfied for the population as a whole. Stage 5 consciousness is a phenomenal aspect that arises in those participants of the loop who simultaneously satisfy the conditions of stage 4. For them, V becomes two-level, and the trace layer is formed through the coupling of their self-overlay with the accumulated traces in Y. Without the conditions of stage 4, the circuit operates, but there is no trace layer of V, because there is no V at all.

**The retention mechanism at stage 5: distribution through duplication.** At stages 1-4, retention mechanisms operated within a single system. At stage 5, retention becomes distributed: the accumulated population model is retained through multiple duplication of carriers and through material structures in Y that outlive individual carriers. The death of a single carrier or the destruction of a single material trace does not destroy the accumulated model if it is represented in others. Loss occurs only with the systemic destruction of a large part of the population and its material infrastructure simultaneously. This is qualitatively more powerful than all previous retention mechanisms and simultaneously introduces a new type of vulnerability - to the destruction of the circuit's infrastructure.

**The probabilistic nature of the transition**. Conditions (a)-(d) are necessary. Their fulfillment requires: sufficient stability of physical traces in Y; an interaction structure ensuring the regular incorporation of traces into the modeling of other carriers; conditions under which traces reconstruct V-models, rather than merely channeling behavior; a mechanism for generating new traces by the restructured models. All four are probabilistically sufficient. The transition 4→5 is significantly rarer than the transition 3→4: the overwhelming majority of stage 4 populations do not develop a complete M↔Y loop. This is consistent with the fact that stage 5 is the rarest and narrowest funnel in the entire ladder.

**What is excluded and what is included.** Populations of stage 4 systems that do not meet conditions (a)-(d) remain at stage 4. The channelling of behaviour through physical traces without restructuring the V-model is a precursor to the loop, not stage 5. Empirically, in its complete form, Level 5 has been represented by Homo sapiens since the emergence of language and, even more so, writing. In a partial form - several species with local transmission of traces (whales with an acoustic culture, some primates, corvids with the transmission of tool-using techniques). The boundary here is empirically blurred because the structural conditions (especially (c) - restructuring of the V-model - and (d) - generation of new traces by restructured models) are difficult to measure in an external system.

**Substrate neutrality of stage 5.** The specific physical forms of traces vary with the substrate in which the M↔Y circuit operates. In biological populations , traces are chemical markers, physical artifacts, and behavioral patterns recorded in the environment. Hypothetically, in information-causal systems, traces may be stable information structures in the general environment of the systems - records, database states, texts, any information-causal traces; the implementation of the M↔Y circuit in this substrate is empirically open and is discussed in Section 10.3. In mixed systems - a combination. Structurally, the same M↔Y circuit operates in all cases; only the physical forms of trace implementation differ.

**Macro-models of transition.** A full discussion is provided in the supplementary chapter on macro-models. Here is a brief list. Conceptual: language as the operating system of a population (a pack of wolves versus a human tribe). Physical: the history of humanity as observed in historical chronicles as a recursion with exponential leaps (writing, the printing press, digital technologies); a parallel transformation of Earth's physical environment at a rate several orders of magnitude faster than biological evolution. Computational: models of cultural evolution and the replication of units of information in populations of agents.

## 3.6. The probabilistic nature of the algorithm

The ladder described in sections 3.1-3.5 is not a deterministic sequence of transitions. This requires explicit formal articulation, because understanding this structure determines how to interpret the entire theory.

**The structure of the conditions for each transition.** For each of the transitions 1-4, minimal conditions are formulated in the form of lists (a), (b), (c), and so on. All conditions in each list are necessary: without the fulfillment of any of them, the transition is impossible. However, in none of the transitions are the conditions sufficient in a deterministic sense. Their simultaneous fulfillment in the system of the previous step does not guarantee a transition to the next; it makes the transition possible with some probability, depending on the specific states of the system and the environment.

Formally, this means the following. Let N_n be the set of necessary conditions for a transition from stage n to stage n+1. The fulfillment of N_n in system S places it in a transition-possible state. The realization of the transition in this state is a stochastic process with a certain probability p_n, depending on specific parameters. Most systems that find themselves in the transition-possible mode do not realize the transition. A minority do. This is consistent with the mathematical structure of phase transitions in physics: under critical conditions, the transition becomes possible, but at each point in the system it occurs or does not occur stochastically.

Structurally, the probabilistic nature of each transition follows from the operation of the consolidation mechanism (preamble to Section 3 and Subsection 3.7). Consolidation operates where there is a difference and there are configurations capable of realizing it. The emergence of a new type of configuration at the next stage requires the coincidence of several independent conditions: suitable gradient physics, sufficient density of possible configurations, and sufficient time for the statistical emergence of a closed structure. Each of these conditions has its own independent probability; their joint fulfillment is the product of these probabilities. This is not a randomness of the process as such, but a structural consequence of the fact that consolidation in each new form requires a narrower coincidence of conditions than consolidation in the previous one. At the 1→2 stage, the conditions for the chemistry of a closed loop coincide. At the 2→3 stage, the conditions for the chemistry of a closed loop coincide, plus the conditions for the presence in Y of regularities to which predictive correlation is advantageous. At the 3→4 stage, the previous conditions coincide, plus the conditions for the recursion of subsystem M onto the system itself. And so on. Each subsequent type of consolidation imposes additional conditions on the previous ones, and the joint coincidence of all conditions becomes statistically increasingly rare.

**The funnel of stages.** From the probabilistic nature of each transition, it follows that the ladder as a whole has a funnel-like structure: the higher the stage, the narrower the set of systems located on it.

Stage 1 (dissipative structure) - is extremely common in the universe. It arises wherever there is an energy gradient across an open system. Stars, planetary atmospheric dynamics, chemical systems - there are billions of examples.

Stage 2 (autopoiesis) - many orders of magnitude rarer. It arose once on Earth (or several times with a single surviving lineage); in the Solar System, no traces of its independent emergence outside Earth have yet been detected.

Stage 3 (proto-agency) - has arisen independently many times within Earth's biosphere and is widespread; outside Earth - unknown. Relative to the universe as a whole - a rare phenomenon.

Stage 4 (consciousness) - within the Earth's biosphere, several dozen species have apparently reached this stage, predominantly among mammals, with limited instances among birds and cephalopods. The overwhelming majority of proto-agent lineages did not reach Stage 4.

Stage 5 (recursively complexifying conscious system) - on Earth, one species has fully passed this stage. Several others emerged in partial forms but did not become established.

This funnel is not a random empirical observation. It is a direct consequence of the architecture of consolidation: the higher the stage, the greater the number of conditions that must coincide for consolidation to work in a new form, and the more specific each of these conditions becomes. The structure of the funnel is determined not by "decreasing probability" as an abstract property, but by the accumulating narrowness of the conditions under which consolidation works. Each subsequent type of consolidation requires the existence of all previous types plus additional structural conditions specific to its stage. Therefore, the funnel is a structural object, not a statistical aberration.

What this changes in the interpretation of the theory. The probabilistic nature of the algorithm resolves several potential misunderstandings.

First. The theory does not claim that any system with an energy gradient inevitably becomes conscious. The opposite is claimed: most systems stop at lower stages, and the transition to each subsequent stage is a rare event.

Second. The theory does not claim that consciousness is the "goal" or "direction" of the process of increasing complexity. It asserts that consciousness is one of the possible outcomes at one of the upper steps of the ladder; its realization at any specific point in the universe depends on a stochastic convergence of conditions.

Third. The theory does not predict that artificial systems will automatically transition to the next steps as computational power increases. The transition from 3 to 4 requires a structural event of self-overlay of a latent invariant of an agentic causal node, and this does not occur automatically as system parameters grow. It requires specific architectural properties, including its own Y and a bidirectional M↔Y loop with its own traces (Section 10.3). Exactly which architectures will lead to its realization is an open question; the theory formulates criteria but does not predict timelines.

Fourth. The theory is consistent with the anthropic principle without requiring it separately. If the transition 4 → 5 is the narrowest funnel of the ladder, then observers at step 5 are, by definition, rare. We view the universe from a position in which a rare transition occurred; the fact that this position appears exceptional is a direct consequence of its rarity, not a property of the universe as a whole.

**Connection to the physics of phase transitions.** The probabilistic nature of transitions between steps is structurally analogous to first-order phase transitions in physics. In the critical region where the conditions are satisfied, the transition becomes possible but not mandatory; at each point in the system, it occurs stochastically; statistically, it occurs in a certain fraction of the system and not in the rest; the critical conditions themselves are defined formally, but the realization of the transition at each specific point remains probabilistic.

Here, it is necessary to distinguish between two levels of this connection.

At the level of formal structure, transitions between the steps of the ladder possess the same properties as first-order phase transitions in physics: a critical region where conditions are satisfied, stochastic realization, statistical distribution across the ensemble, and accumulation of the statistical density of suitable configurations up to a critical point, beyond which the transition to a new regime becomes physically possible. This formal structure is the general mechanism in which the work of consolidation (preamble to Section 3) is concretely realized at each step: consolidation accumulates the density of suitable configurations; upon reaching the critical density, the transition becomes possible; the realization of the transition at each point is stochastic; on average across the ensemble, the transition occurs in a certain fraction of systems.

This is a structural identity grounded in the general formalism of the theory of critical phenomena (Stanley, 1971; Sornette, 2006), and it makes the use of the language of phase transitions in this work not an analogy, but an application of the general formalism to a new domain. At the level of the physical mechanism, however, transitions between the steps of the ladder and physical phase transitions (water-vapor, Curie point, cosmological transitions) are different concrete realizations of this general formalism. The microscopic mechanism of our ladder - the establishment of a coupling of structural conditions in the system upon stochastic fulfillment of the necessary requirements - cannot be reduced to molecular dynamics or to spontaneous symmetry breaking. Therefore, when the paper states that "this structure operates on molecular, magnetic, cosmological, and our scales," it refers to a general formalism of critical phenomena, not to a single physical process. The universality of this structure is one aspect of the structural self-similarity of the entire pattern, which operates at the level of molecular systems (water-vapor), at the level of magnetic systems (Curie point), at the level of cosmological transitions in the early Universe, and - in our theory - at the level of transitions between stages of the emergence of consciousness. The universality of this structure is one aspect of the structural self-similarity of the entire pattern presented in this work: the phase transition as a mechanism operates identically on scales ranging from molecular systems to cosmological ones, and each level of our ladder is its realization on a scale specific to that level. The complete assembly of the structural picture is in subsection 3.7.

An analogy with physical phase transitions leads to one important implication that must be explicitly stated. During a phase transition, the properties of the system change qualitatively, and the appropriate variables used to describe it also change. Liquid water is described by equations for a liquid; vapor - by equations for a gas; no one demands a "single formula linking the parameters of liquid water to those of vapor" in the sense of a continuous transition of variables. The connection between the two states is provided by the thermodynamics of phase transitions - the theory of the conditions under which one state is replaced by another. Structurally, the same situation applies in our framework. At stage 1, the thermodynamic variables of the dissipative structure are relevant. At stage 2 - the parameters of a closed causal loop in the autocatalytic set. At stage 3, the generative model and variational free energy are relevant. At stage 4, the self-representation structure with variable V is relevant. At stage 5, the dynamics of model recursion in the population are relevant. The theory does not require a single equation that transforms the parameters of one stage into the parameters of another; the theory requires conditions under which the system transitions from one regime to another, and these conditions are given in Sections 3.2-3.5. This is a structure of the same type as in the theory of phase transitions - not a "single language for all states," but "rules for switching between states." The objection that the ladder lacks a unified formalism is based on an implicit expectation of a continuous, uninterrupted description. The physics of phase transitions is not structured that way, and our ladder, which replicates its structure, should not be structured that way either.

**The internal logic of the ladder** lies beyond the probabilistic structure. The probabilistic nature of transitions and the funnel structure define the formal framework of the ladder. Behind this framework lies a substantive internal logic - the operation of the theory's four cross-cutting elements (Y, the "gradient → retention → pole → transition" pattern, consolidation, emergent time) as they are applied to differences of ever-increasing structural depth: the sequential accumulation of specific types of gradients, the accumulation of increasingly stable mechanisms of resistance to decay, the sequential expansion of the scale of gradient localization, the unfolding of activity through three phases (temporal → directed V → distributed), structural linking of the phenomenon to the disruption of inherited gradients via V. This logic is a unified pattern through which the theory describes all the processes it encompasses, and its construction is the task of the next subsection.

## 3.7. The Internal Logic of the Ladder: Gradient, Accumulation, Structural Self-Similarity

Sections 3.1-3.6 unfold the formal structure of the ladder: steps and operations, transitions and their minimal conditions, the probabilistic nature of realization, and reconciliation with the physics of phase transitions. This is sufficient for the ladder to function as a formal construct. It is not, however, sufficient for it to function as a unified picture. Without an assembly of internal logic, the reader traverses the ladder as a sequence of steps, held together by a formal analogy with phase transitions, but without understanding what exactly unfolds through this sequence as a unified process. This subsection brings this logic together.

The assembly is carried out through six observations, each of which emerged during the analysis of individual transitions in 3.2-3.5 and was recorded there in short subsections. Here they are gathered into a general structure, and through this assembly the structural self-similarity of the pattern, stated in Section 2 as the central thesis of the work, is revealed.

### 3.7.1. The Gradient as a Permeating Structural Invariant

Before unfolding the pervasive nature of the gradient through the ladder, it is necessary to clarify in what sense the term is used in this work. In its ordinary mathematical sense, a gradient is a vector of partial derivatives of a scalar field - a formal object describing the direction and rate of change of a quantity in space. In the ordinary physical sense, it is a spatial difference in a quantity that generates a flow (a temperature gradient generates heat conduction, a concentration gradient generates diffusion, and a potential gradient generates a current). Both meanings are special cases of a more general concept in which the gradient is used in this work and which will now be formulated.

In the framework proposed here, a gradient is a state of non-equilibrium of a system - a stable distinction between two possibilities through which the system is structured and evolves. This distinction may be spatial (between two points in the environment), but need not be so. It may be between two alternative states of a single system (structured / homogeneous), between two architectures (closed / open), between two tempos (internal dynamics / environmental), between two ontological possibilities of the system as a whole (holding together / falling apart), between two historical states of a supra-individual structure (M*n / M*{n+1}). All these cases are gradients in the same overarching structural sense.

This is what unites them as a single object. In all cases, a gradient is a stable distinction that cannot be reduced to an instantaneous state and generates dynamics. It is not a vector as a formal structure, nor a difference in magnitudes as a quantitative measure, but a mode of the system's existence in a state of tension between two possibilities. Without such tension, the system either reaches equilibrium (spatial gradient), or homogeneity (structural), or synchrony with the environment (temporal), or disintegration (ontological), or generational stagnation (historical). With such tension, it exists and develops. Each of the theory's gradients is a state, not an object.

The ladder reveals exactly how this tension is realized at each scale. At each subsequent level, the carrier of differentiation changes - that is, the specific entities between which the gradient operates. At level 0, the medium is the environment in which two points with different values of a physical quantity exist. At level 1, it is the system itself, in which two alternative modes of its existence differ under a given flow. At level 2, it is the internal architecture of the system, in which closed and open causal configurations differ. At stage 3, it is the system's relationship with the environment, in which their rates differ. At stage 4, it is the system as a whole in its ontological dimension, in which its preservation and decay differ. At stage 5, it is a structure transcending the individual system, in which its historical states differ.

Each subsequent type of gradient is deeper not in the sense of being "more abstract," but in the sense that it operates at a deeper level of what exactly constitutes the medium of differentiation. First, the external environment. Then - the system itself in its internal organization. Then - its relationship with the environment. Then - its own existence as a whole. And finally - the structure in which individual systems are participants, not carriers in their entirety. This is a sequential expansion of the scale of localization, which will be specifically discussed in 3.7.3.

With this definition, we turn to the sequence of gradient types unfolding through the ladder. At step 0, an energy gradient operates in the environment. At step 1 - the same gradient plus a stability gradient between the structured and homogeneous states at a given flow rate. At step 2 - the same two plus the structural gradient between a closed causal loop and an open chain. At step 3 - the same three plus the temporal gradient between the rates of internal dynamics and environmental dynamics. At stage 4 - the same four plus the ontological gradient V between "holding on" and "falling apart" in a system-specific sense. At stage 5 - the same five plus a sixth, between historical states of the supra-individual structure.

The gradient here is not merely one of the theory's terms. It is an object that manifests itself at each level in a form specific to that level, and through the succession of these forms, the ladder acquires internal unity. Each transition is not a transition to a new step in some general sense, but to a new type of gradient added to those already existing. The ladder is a sequential complication of the very thing in which the gradient is realized.

### 3.7.2. The Ladder as an Accumulation: Gradients and Retention Mechanisms

From 3.7.1 follows the first substantive property of the ladder: it is a structure of accumulation, not a sequence. Each subsequent step does not replace the previous one, but incorporates it and adds its own new gradient. Step 5 is not a separate, high step - it is a composition of six gradients, in which the first five are inherited and function as conditions for the existence of the sixth. A disruption of any lower gradient rolls the system back down: upon the destruction of a closed loop, the system returns to step 1; upon the destruction of form - to step 0; upon loss of V - to stage 3. The stability of each stage depends on the stability of all lower stages, and this aligns with the empirical reality of biological death: the death of an organism (loss of V) does not negate the fact that the biochemistry of its components continues to function for some time (stages 1 and 2 break down later).

Parallel to the accumulation of gradients is the accumulation of mechanisms of resistance to decay. At stage 1 - hysteresis: the system's ability to remain in a structured state for some time after the flow drops below the critical level. At stage 2 - causal self-sufficiency of a closed loop: independence from specific external components. At stage 3 - active alignment of the environment with the model: for the first time, the system does not merely survive in the environment but transforms it. At stage 4 - preemptive planning: action based on a model of a possible future that includes the system's own potential non-existence. At stage 5 - distribution through multiple duplication of carriers and material structures that outlive individual carriers.

Each subsequent mechanism is qualitatively more powerful than the previous one. And - fundamentally - at stage 5, the retention mechanism extends beyond the boundaries of a single system for the first time. Up to stage 5, retention was a property of the system as such; at stage 5, it becomes a property of the population and its material products. This is a qualitative shift, which we will address specifically in 3.7.3.

### 3.7.3. Sequence of gradient types: expansion of the scale of localization

When examining the types of gradients in their sequence, one discovers not random diversity but a structural shift. The type of the new gradient at each stage shifts as follows:

Step 0 - spatial gradient in the medium.

Stage 1 - between alternative states of the system (structured / homogeneous).

Stage 2 - between alternative system architectures (closed loop / open circuit).

Stage 3 - between rates (internal dynamics / environmental dynamics).

Stage 4 - between ontological states of the system as a whole (holding together / disintegrating).

Stage 5 - between historical states of the supra-individual structure (M*n / M*{n+1}).

This sequence encompasses the expansion of the scale on which the gradient is localized. First, the gradient operates within the environment relative to the system (stage 0). Then - at the boundary between the system and the environment (stage 1). Then - within the system as a structure (stage 2). Then - between the system's internal dynamics and the environment (stage 3). Then - between two possibilities of the system itself as a whole (stage 4). And finally - beyond the boundaries of a single system, between states of the structure that transcends it (stage 5).

This is not merely the emergence of new dimensions; it is a sequential expansion of the scope within which the gradient operates. From points in the environment to distinctions within a single system and further beyond the boundaries of an individual system - into the population and its history. The qualitative shift at stage 5, noted in 3.5, is not a coincidence in this logic, but a natural continuation of an accumulating trend: the expansion of the scale of localization reaches the limit at which the gradient can no longer be contained within a single system.

The expansion of the scale of localization to this limit signifies not the exit of anything beyond the substrate, but the emergence of a substrate of a new, higher order: a supra-individual structure whose components are complete conscious carriers of stage 4 together with their traces in Y. The relation of stage 5 to stage 4 here is the same as that of an organism to a cell: a component of the higher substrate is itself a complete carrier of the lower stage, and the higher substrate is a network of such components that holds its accumulated model across the turnover of carriers. The pole of this structure is structural (the restructuring of the successor's V-model); whether the supra-individual structure has its own experience the theory does not decide here - phenomenal V remains on the biological layer of each carrier.

The same criterion also determines the upper boundary of the ladder. The ladder continues exactly as far as there exists a physically real (not mathematically constructible) next scale of localization at which a pole of a new type is named. A stage beyond the trans-individual one is declared only when its pole is named; amplifying the effect of an existing stage without a change in the type of pole is not a transition. The openness of the ladder at the top is therefore not a gap of imagination but a substantive claim: the next pole is not named at the accessible physically real scales, and the closure of the sequence at the achieved stage is a position to be defended, not a caveat.

### 3.7.4. The Formation of Activity Through Three Phases

Activity, defined as a system's ability to transform its environment, does not emerge immediately - it unfolds in a three-phase process, each phase linked to the emergence of a corresponding gradient.

The first phase - at stage 3 - involves a temporal gradient. Only a system possessing internal dynamics that differ in pace from those of the environment is capable of retaining past states and modeling possible futures. From this retention arises the ability to act - to bring the environment into alignment with the model. The temporal gradient is the first "active" gradient: at stages 1 and 2, retention was passive (form, hysteresis, closed loop), and the system did not intervene in the environment. At stage 3, it intervenes for the first time.

The second phase occurs at stage 4, via the ontological gradient V. Activity here acquires directionality. The proto-agent acts to bring the environment into alignment with the model of the current gradient; the conscious system acts to maintain itself in the state V = "I am maintaining," and all other actions are directed through this. These are different things. A bacterium moves toward glucose because its signaling network is configured that way; there is no background pole there. The conscious system holds itself on the verge of disappearance as the structural pole of all activity, and activity acquires not merely a capacity, but directed content - it serves a purpose, in the technical sense of the word.

The third phase occurs at stage 5, through the distribution of the sixth gradient. Activity ceases to belong to a single agent. It functions as the coordinated action of a multitude of carriers through a shared accumulated model. Each individual agent of stage 5 retains their individual activity from stage 4 (their V and directionality belong to them), but the accumulated model develops through the sum of the contributions of many agents and their interactions. It is from this distribution that the exponential rate of environmental transformation arises, distinguishing stage 5 from everything that came before: acceleration is a structural consequence of activity transitioning from the mode of the individual agent to the mode of distributed recursion.

This three-phase unfolding of activity - temporal → directed V → distributed - is one of the supporting lines of the ladder. Through it, the work's first authorial thesis (consciousness as an active mechanism of complication) receives structural justification: activity, as a pervasive property, unfolds through the ladder, and at stage 5 reaches the scale at which it becomes the primary factor in the transformation of the system and the environment.

### 3.7.5. The Presence of Inherited Gradients in V as a Mechanism of the Phenomenon

At steps 1-3, gradient disruptions occur with the system as external events: the system disintegrates, depletes, and loses its ability to act. The system has no internal position relative to which these disruptions would become something for it. At step 4, through the emergence of V, such a position arises. Violations of inherited gradients begin to be present in V - to become, for the system, something relative to its maintenance. Hunger, pain, anxiety, and fear (fully analyzed in 3.4) are essentially the ways in which violations of inherited gradients acquire experiential content through V at stage 4. These states - the phenomenal content of stage 4 - are structurally necessary modes of presence in which the disruptions of each of the inherited gradients acquire experiential content.

A full justification of this thesis is presented in 3.4. Here, we indicate its place within the general internal logic of the ladder. Phenomenal content does not arise "out of nowhere" upon reaching complexity and is not a separate class of phenomena beyond the structure. It is a necessary consequence of the emergence of V as a pole in the system, inheriting the gradients of the preceding steps. Through the presence in V, the ladder connects its structural side with the phenomenal one: one is the inner side of the other, and the connection occurs at step 4 through a specific mechanism formalized in this work. At step 5, this structure of presence becomes more complex due to the two-level nature of V (section 3.5): to the biological layer of V, inherited from stage 4, a trace layer of V is added, formed through the bidirectional circuit M↔Y with the accumulated model; the presence of inherited gradients through V in the carrier of stage 5 is distributed between both layers, and threats may arise in each of them independently or simultaneously.

This provides a structural grounding for the philosophical thesis regarding the identity of structure and phenomenon (Section 6). It is not that "structure is in some way identical to phenomenon," but rather that "structure is present to itself through V at stage 4, and this presence is phenomenal content." Identity acquires operational content, not remaining merely an ontological declaration.

### 3.7.6. Structural Self-Similarity of the Pattern

The six observations above - gradient as an invariant, accumulation, expansion of the scale of localization, three-phase activity, presence through V - come together into a single overall structure. This structure is the four-phase pattern "gradient → retention → pole → transition," operating at every level of the ladder and across the scales encompassed by the work as a whole.

Before applying the pattern's operation across different scales, it is necessary to explicitly specify relative to what each of its four elements operates. Without such a reference, the pattern remains internally formal, and each element hangs in the air: gradient in what, retention relative to what, pole relative to what, transition to where. All four elements of the pattern operate relative to Y - the environment variable introduced in the preamble to Section 3. The gradient is a stable distinction within Y, manifesting in different forms at different stages: a spatial distinction within Y at stage 0, a distinction between alternative states of the system within Y at stage 1, a distinction between the system's architectures regarding its exchange with Y at stage 2, a distinction between the pace of the system's internal dynamics and the pace of the accessible aspect of Y at stage 3, a distinction between two possibilities of the system as a whole regarding its retention in Y at stage 4, a distinction between states of the supra-individual structure within the trace layer of Y at stage 5. Retention is the resistance to the system's disintegration with respect to its position in Y and with respect to the aspect of Y accessible to it; retention mechanisms accumulate across the stages precisely as forms of such resistance (thermodynamic hysteresis, causal self-sufficiency, active alignment of Y with the model, preventive planning regarding V in Y, distribution through the trace layer Y). A pole is a structural configuration relative to which the system's retention in Y is realized and through which all its causal exchanges with Y are organized: at stages 1-3, this is the structural stability of the retention carrier; at stage 4, it is V in self-representation - the distinction "holding together / disintegrating" over the carrier's own configuration; at stage 5, it is a distinction of a new type, over the model rather than over the carrier's configuration: whether the V-model of the subsequent configuration has been restructured through a physical trace in Y, or only its behavior has been channeled (a stigmergy proto-form), or the trace has been lost (Section 3.5). The two-level character of the V of a stage-5 carrier (a biological layer plus a trace layer) describes retention - what the carrier holds; the pole of stage 5 is the distinction over the successor's model itself, not the two-level character as such. A transition is a change in the system's access spectrum to Y - the acquisition of an architectural capacity for causal exchange with that aspect of Y which was previously inaccessible to the system. Y enters the pattern not as a fifth element, but as a cross-cutting variable relative to which the other four operate. This gives the pattern a formal foundation and simultaneously gives Y its functional role within the theoretical framework: Y does not describe something separate; it structures what is described by all the other elements of the pattern.

At each stage, the pattern repeats: a level-specific gradient emerges (or previous gradients are retained and accumulated); the system sustains itself by working with this gradient and through all inherited mechanisms of self-sustainment; at stage 4, an explicit V-pole appears; at the preceding stages, its proto-forms appear (the distinction between "this form / decay" at stage 1, the closed loop at stage 2, the maintenance of the model at stage 3); and at stage 5, a pole of a new type is added on top of the full V-pole - the distinction of the restructuring of the successor's V-model (Section 3.5); and then - the transition to the next step or the closing of the cycle.

The same pattern operates at scales where the ladder manifests as a whole:

\- Within a single step. Each step, on its own micro-scale, follows a four-phase logic: formation of a gradient specific to it → maintaining the system through this gradient → stabilization (with the proto-form of the pole) → the possibility of transitioning to the next step.

\- At the level of the staircase as a whole. Six gradients accumulate → step 4 yields a distinct pole V → on steps 5 and beyond, this pole is distributed and (on the speculative horizon of section 7) inverted upon the cycle's closure. The ladder as a whole follows the same four-phase pattern.

\- Within step 5 - on short generational cycles. Each generation receives the accumulated model as starting material (gradient) → retains and enriches it → at the end of its life passes it on to the next generation (in a local sense - inversion of a single carrier's pole through the transition of the accumulated structure to the next generation) → a new cycle begins.

\- At the level of historical cultural cycles within stage 5. An epoch undergoes a cycle from the activated state of trace layer V (accumulation and tension) through a balanced state (a dense framework with dissipated tension - a four-phase pole before the transition) to restructuring via catastrophe or renewal and the beginning of a new cycle. This fourth scale - between generational microcycles and the cosmological scale - ly establishes structural self-similarity as a structural property of the entire process covered by the theory, leaving no gaps between levels.

This is the structural self-similarity of the "gradient → retention → pole → transition" pattern. I must explicitly clarify in what sense it works and in what sense it does not. The self-similarity I am asserting here is not geometric fractality in the strict mathematical sense - that is, it is not invariance with respect to scaling with a fractal dimension in the sense of Hausdorff or some other strict measure. It is a structural isomorphism between levels, possessing a certain strength and certain boundaries.

What is common across all scales are the four formal elements of the pattern. At each level, there is a gradient (a source of tension around which the system forms); there is retention (a mechanism through which the system resists disintegration relative to the gradient); there is a pole (a stable structural configuration around which retention is realized); and there is a transition (the condition under which the system transforms into the system of the next level). These four elements constitute the general formal schema of the pattern, and their joint presence at every stage and on every scale covered by the work constitutes a substantive statement, not a mere analogy.

What differs across different scales is the substantive realization of each of the four elements. The type of gradient shifts from spatial (thermodynamic gradient of dissipative structures) through chemical (concentration gradients of autocatalytic cycles) and temporal (differing rates of modeling and environment in the proto-agent) to ontological (the "I am retained / disintegrate" pole in the stage 4 carrier) and further to the interpopulation and historical (trace layer V in stage 5). The type of retention changes accordingly - from thermodynamic hysteresis to modeling self-reference. The type of pole changes from the structural stability of a dissipative structure to a sustained modeling process. The transition conditions differ at each level and are formulated separately for each transition in subsections 3.2-3.5.

This is precisely the structural isomorphism of a certain kind: a general four-element scheme realized at different scales with different content. The universality of the structure of phase transitions in physics, noted in 3.6, is a manifestation of this isomorphism - phase transitions reproduce a four-cycle pattern on scales ranging from molecular to cosmological, with different physical content in each cycle. Self-similarity functions as a methodological tool justifying the transfer of apparatus and methods from one stage of to another: the difference test with a zero model, developed in subsection 10.2 for the 3→4 transition, is in principle applicable to other transitions following the same general scheme; the formalism of critical phenomena, which works on certain scales, is justifiably applied to others. Not a "strict fractal," but certainly a structurally isomorphic pattern, and this precise formulation is the correct place for the theory.

This self-similarity does not only describe - it forbids, and in this lies its difference from descriptive theories of self-organization. Synergetics and general systems theory record the similarity of patterns across scales as an observed regularity but do not forbid an alternative form of transition. The present theory makes a stronger claim: the form of a vertical transition is forced. A vertical transition - a change in the type of pole - realized otherwise than through the full four-element pattern "gradient → retention → pole → transition" (without a gradient, or without a retention phase, or without a pole, or without a change in the access spectrum to Y), the theory declares impossible. This is a falsifiable predicate: the discovery of a vertical transition of a different form refutes not a single stage but the unity of the ladder as a causal law. The claim concerns the form of a transition, not its occurrence: whether a transition occurs is stochastic (Section 3.6), but if it occurs, its form is forced. The predicate specifies concrete forbidden forms. A pole of a new type that arises without a preceding gradient is forbidden. A pole of a new type that has not passed through a retention phase - a configuration that momentarily exhibited a distinction of a higher type and disintegrated without consolidating it - is a fluctuation, not the crossing of a stage, and as a transition is forbidden. A pole of a new type without the acquisition of a new access spectrum to Y is forbidden. Each of these forms is conceivable and yet excluded by the theory; this is why the predicate is substantive rather than a restatement of the observation.

The predicate is in force only within a clearly delimited domain, and this boundary is the condition of its lawfulness, not a caveat. The domain of action: dissipative self-sustaining systems and retention-type transitions - vertical ones, with a change in the type of pole. Outside the domain, and therefore not counterexamples to the predicate, are two classes. The first: equilibrium structures. A crystal grown at equilibrium has no flow through it, hence no gradient, and does not stand on the ladder - it fails the very first element of the pattern. The second: intra-stage (horizontal) reorganization - the complication or restructuring of a system without a change in the type of pole, as well as change under a purely external parameter without a boundary of retention selected from within. Such changes are real, but they are not vertical transitions, and the predicate does not extend to them; their subject is the theory of dynamical systems and bifurcations, not the present theory. It is essential that the boundary is drawn by criteria already operating in the apparatus - flow and gradient, retention, the type of pole - and not introduced to handle particular counterexamples; this is what distinguishes it from an ad hoc reservation.

Horizontal reorganization, while not being a vertical transition (above), can nonetheless raise the internal gradient of the level - for example, the disparity in the rates of the system's internal dynamics and environmental dynamics at stage 3 (Section 3.7.3) - up to the threshold at which a vertical transition becomes possible. It is the internal gradient that is amplified, not the external energy flux, which under complexification, according to Section 2, rather relaxes; the transition itself remains a separate event with its own stochastic condition (Section 3.6), and its dynamics as a process of climbing are not formalized here.

### 3.7.7. Consolidation as a cross-cutting mechanism of accumulation

Section 3.7 described how gradient types, retention mechanisms, localization scales, and forms of activity accumulate through the ladder. All these accumulation processes rely on a single common mechanism that runs through all steps: the consolidation of successful configurations relative to Y. Consolidation is the third of the four cross-cutting elements of the theory (preamble to Section 3) and functions as a structural mechanism that implements the accumulation of complexity at each step.

Formal content of the mechanism. At each step of the ladder, among the multitude of physically possible configurations, a subset of configurations realizes the difference of that step stably - that is, reproduces its structure faster than it dissipates in Y. These configurations are physically retained. Some configurations realize the difference in an unstable manner - they dissipate faster than they are reproduced. These configurations physically disintegrate. This is consolidation in its minimal form: not selection in the sense of choice, but a structural event in which configurations of the first type continue to exist, while configurations of the second type disappear. Consolidation operates where there is a difference and there are configurations capable of realizing it. If there is no difference, consolidation has nothing to work with. If configurations that stably realize the difference do not arise, consolidation has no result.

Substrate neutrality of the principle of consolidation. Structurally, consolidation is the same at all levels, but its physical realization is substrate-specific. In thermodynamic systems (stage 1), consolidation operates through the differential stability of attractors: configurations that are physically stable relative to the flow in Y are retained longer than physically unstable configurations. In biological systems with autopoiesis (stages 2-5), consolidation operates through the difference between the loop's self-reproduction rate and the rate at which it is destroyed by the environment, with evolutionary accumulation over many cycles. In information-causal systems, consolidation operates through the adjustment of the configuration via feedback from the information environment Y, of which the carriers of the full V are a part. In all three cases, there is a single structural logic: the difference operates, and configurations that realize it stably become consolidated. This is the substrate neutrality of the principle of consolidation in its operational form.

Connection to the principle of maximum entropy production. Its formulation in thermodynamic terms (Step 1) is consistent with the principle of maximum entropy production in non-equilibrium thermodynamics (Swenson, 1989; Schneider & Sagan, 2005): dissipative structures are fixed, in part, because they physically accelerate the total entropy production in the system plus Y compared to unstructured configurations. In subsequent steps, the consolidation operates through analogous structural effects specific to each substrate: acceleration of the turnover of organic molecules in the autocatalytic loop, acceleration of the correction of the discrepancy between the model and Y in active inference, acceleration of the retention of V through anticipatory behavioral restructuring, acceleration of the accumulation of the population model through the bidirectional M↔Y loop. In all cases, a single structural effect is at work: a configuration that accelerates the realization of the difference is physically better retained than a configuration that slows down its realization.

The property of consolidation: complexity provides stability. At each stage, a configuration with greater complexity realizes differences through a greater number of structural paths simultaneously. Physically, this means that the loss of a single path does not destroy the entire configuration; a configuration with lower complexity is more likely to collapse upon the loss of a path. As a result, all else being equal, complex configurations are more stable than simple ones - not as a matter of "success," but as a physical property of the multiplicity of ways to realize differences through the configuration.
