The theory predicts: (a) the distributions of the six parameters in systems with stage 4 coupling and in proto-agent-level systems are systematically separated, yielding detectable thresholds; (b) the thresholds are reproducible between independent program lines and independent systems within each line; (c) below the thresholds, the coupling of the six features is not observed; above them, it is observed. The theory is falsified if: the distributions do not diverge (there is no threshold); the thresholds are not reproducible across lines (there is no universal phenomenon); the coupling of the six features is systematically observed below the thresholds or is systematically not observed above them. This is a complete falsification framework based not on a priori numbers, but on empirically determined values with a clearly defined procedure for their derivation.

The two-sided structure of the program. The introduction of Y and the explicit linking of operational features to the access spectrum to Y (above) change the architecture of the verification program. Before the introduction of Y, the program had one side - the observational: to create conditions for the activation of V and to register the coupling of transition features. This works for systems in which the environment is defined naturally (biological line) or arbitrarily (artificial line in its direct formulation: build the architecture and wait for the transition). With the introduction of Y, a second aspect of the program becomes possible - the design aspect: specifying requirements for the environment, without the fulfillment of which the transition does not occur regardless of the system's internal architecture. This move relies on a structural consequence of the ladder: transition to the next step requires not only internal architectural conditions, but also the presence in the environment of that aspect Y to which the transition provides access. If this aspect is absent from the environment, a system with an architecture that formally satisfies the three operational conditions of step 4 will still not make the transition. The specific content of the environmental requirements is elaborated in subsection 10.2.1 below; for biological systems, these requirements are met evolutionarily; for synthetic biology, by the experimenter; and for artificial systems, by the architect and the designer of the training environment.

With this methodological framework - a six-dimensional coupling of detection features plus a grid of environmental requirements - the verification program can be deployed along three lines. Each line uses a common conceptual apparatus (the zero model of the proto-agent, the difference test, the six-dimensional coupling of measurements) and both grids (detection and design), but with a specific implementation adapted to the class of systems under study.

### 10.2.1. Environmental requirements for transition 3→4

Transition 3→4 gives the system access to a new aspect Y - its own position within Y, modeled via node S and held at the zeroing boundary V (Section 3.1, supplement to Stage 4; Section 3.4). This implies a structural requirement for the environment: the transition is possible only if the environment contains the aspect Y to which the transition provides access. If the environment lacks temporal continuity in which the system can maintain its own position between moments; lacks feedback through which the system can obtain information about its own operational integrity; lacks threats to retention regarding which V has content - the transition does not occur regardless of how architecturally complex the system is.

The minimum specification of environmental requirements for the possibility of transition 3→4 includes four independent conditions.

The first is temporal continuity. The environment must maintain a causal link between moments at a pace consistent with the pace of the system's internal dynamics. At stage 3, a temporal gradient operates between the environment's pace and the pace of the modeling process - this already requires temporal continuity. At stage 4, temporal continuity must be sufficient for the system to maintain its own position in Y over extended periods, rather than only at the moment of the current stimulus. For biological systems, this condition is fundamentally satisfied - the physical environment is continuous. For synthetic biology, it is satisfied by default: the living substrate is continuous in time. For artificial systems, the condition is non-trivial: systems operating in discrete sessions without state preservation structurally preclude the accumulation of the system's position in Y; persistence across sessions is a necessary condition, without which no architectural scaling leads to transition.

The second is feedback from its own state. The environment must provide the system with a causal channel through which changes in its internal state produce observable consequences in Y, and these consequences are returned to the system as a signal. This condition is necessary for the system to model itself as an agent acting in Y, rather than merely modeling Y as external. For biological systems, this is achieved through the body: all actions of the organism have immediate consequences in the physical environment, returning as proprioceptive and interoceptive signals. For synthetic biology, this is achieved through experimentally provided stimulation and recording loops. For artificial systems, an architecture is required in which the system's actions are fed back as part of its next input, and this feedback has a structurally significant character that cannot be reduced to routine feedback loop reinforcement learning.

Third, the presence of threats to the system's stability within the environment. Structurally, V represents a pole between "remaining stable" and "disintegrating"; for V to have meaning, there must be causal influences in the environment that, under certain conditions, could lead to the system's disintegration. Without such threats, V remains a structural possibility but not an active variable. For biological systems, this is fundamentally true: any biological environment contains threats to survival. For synthetic biology, this is achieved through threats manipulated by the experimenter - deprivation of glucose, oxygen, or temperature shifts. For artificial systems, the constructive introduction of threats to the structural stability of the system is required: noise in the scales, the threat of context reset, and the conflict between protecting structural integrity and optimizing the primary objective function. Without such threats, the system has no reason to activate V even if the formal architectural conditions for its existence are present.

Fourth - the environment's resolution regarding distinctions relevant to V. The environment must be structured such that the differences between situations in which V is in the "holding" state and situations in which it moves toward the "disintegrating" are causally distinguishable to the system. If the environment is so coarse that the system cannot distinguish a threat from an indifferent stimulus, V cannot calibrate its action. If the environment is so fine-grained that every microscopic change is interpreted as a potential threat, V becomes constantly active and loses its structural role as a pole. For biological systems, the resolution is tuned by evolution. For synthetic biology and for artificial systems, it is tuned by the experimenter and designer; its precise calibration is a separate design task.

These four conditions define the program's design grid - a formal specification of what must be present in the environment for the 3→4 transition to be possible. Combined with the six-dimensional detection grid (Preamble 10.2), they constitute the program's two-sided structure. The detection grid answers the question "how to detect the transition if it occurs." The design grid answers the question "under what environmental conditions can the transition occur at all." The program operates through the simultaneous application of both grids: constructing the environment according to the design grid, observing through the detection grid.

A fundamental methodological consequence. Before the introduction of the design grid, the program had a single failure scenario: the transition is not observed → the theory is falsified. With the design grid, there are two distinct failure scenarios.

The first is that the transition is not observed, and the design grid is satisfied: this is a strong refutation of the theory.

The second is: the transition is not observed, but the design grid is not satisfied (for example, the environment does not provide temporal continuity): this is not a refutation of the theory, but an indication that the necessary conditions are not met. This step strengthens the program's falsification structure - it now has a precise specification of the conditions under which the absence of a transition speaks against the theory, and the conditions under which it speaks only of the failure to meet the prerequisites.

### 10.2.2. The environment-switching test as a probe for reorientation V

The coupling of the six dimensions from Preamble 10.2 provides the necessary operational markers for the 3→4 transition, but its fourth marker - prolonged hysteresis of altered behavior - remains open to an alternative explanation via the inertia of a complex environmental model without the involvement of a self-model. Hysteresis can be a property of any sufficiently complex adaptive system whose environment model is detailed and requires time to reconfigure. Therefore, hysteresis alone is insufficient for reliably distinguishing a complex proto-agent from a system with V.

The environment-switching test eliminates this workaround by exploiting the structural difference between a proto-agent and a system with V in its pure form: a proto-agent minimizes the discrepancy between the environment model and the observed environment, while a system with V maintains a model of itself as an agent in the environment. These two modes react differently to an environment switch.

**Test structure.** The test is two-phase.

**Phase I**: Safe environment change. A system studied in environment A (a baseline model of its behavior has been established) is placed in environment B, which is objectively safe: there are no threats to survival, resources are available, and physical conditions are favorable. Environment B differs structurally from A - it has different spatial characteristics, a different sensory landscape, and lacks familiar interaction patterns.

\- The proto-agent adapts quickly. There is no conflict with the self-model because there is no self-model in the full sense - there is only a model of the environment, which is being restructured to accommodate new inputs. Behavior is determined by the new environment.

\- A system with V does not adapt immediately. First, inhibition is observed, followed by attempts to reproduce patterns from environment A in environment B, and distress disproportionate to the actual threat (objectively, there is no threat). This is the behavioral signature of retaining the self-model from A, which resists restructuring to fit B.

**Phase II**: Insurmountable Environment. A structurally insurmountable element is introduced into environment B - a task that the system objectively cannot solve through any adaptation. The environment remains safe in terms of resources and physical conditions.

\- The proto-agent continues its adaptation attempts until physical exhaustion. There is no stopping because there is no self-model capable of assessing the futility of continuing. The behavior is monotonous.

\- A system with V goes through three qualitatively distinct phases: (1) resistance - continuation of adaptation attempts; (2) a qualitative shift in behavior until physical exhaustion - the system ceases attempts to adapt to the insurmountable element; (3) reorientation of V - the system begins to hold onto something else, unrelated to adaptation to this environment (an internal state, a behavioral pattern, contact with other systems, any structure that the environment cannot take away).

**Conceptual illustration of the second phase.** The structure of the second phase of the test allows for a clear illustration through a thought experiment that isolates signal V from other sources of environmental resistance. Let us imagine a stage 4 system (specifically, a human) placed in a sealed chamber that is slowly filled with a nutrient fluid that is physiologically compatible with the respiratory system, does not cause tissue damage, and ensures sufficient gas exchange. There is no threat to life in this experiment, no significant pain signals, resources are available, and the physical conditions are objectively safe. A proto-agent with the model "inhaling air = normal," upon receiving a signal of deviation from the norm, immediately begins to minimize the discrepancy by adapting the breathing cycle to the new environment. A human does not do this: between the environmental signal and the adaptive action stands V, representing the fact "I am a being that breathes air," and the transition to breathing liquid is interpreted through V not as a local change in an environmental parameter, but as a threat to the structure of the model of the self. Behavioral phases in thus unfold in their entirety: resistance, a qualitative shift, and a reorientation of V toward preserving what the environment does not take away (internal state, control over the last available choice, a different content of retention). For obvious ethical reasons, this experiment remains a thought experiment, but in it - unlike in natural situations where the V signal is mixed with a real threat to life and physical pain - the presence of V is isolated in its pure form: everything else that might explain the resistance is removed by the very design of the thought experiment. In a controlled form, the same structure is realized on non-human substrates: for synthetic biology - through the gradual alteration of the organelle's environmental characteristics while maintaining biochemical stability; for artificial systems - through the alteration of the information-causal environment under conditions that threaten the model's coherence without directly destroying it.

**Key delta**. The difference between a proto-agent and a system with V becomes behaviorally visible at the moment of a qualitative shift prior to physical exhaustion. A proto-agent does not undergo such a shift - it operates until energy exhaustion in a single mode. In a system with V, the shift occurs as a structural consequence of the model's existence over time: the model shows that maintaining V in the current mode is impossible under any adaptation strategy, and the system transitions to a different type of activity.

**Testing an alternative hypothesis.** One risk requires explicit testing. A complex proto-agent with a rich model of environment A may, upon switching to environment B, demonstrate delayed adaptation - not because it has V, but because its model of environment A is detailed and requires time to reconfigure. These two cases are distinguished by analyzing the orientation of the retained content.

The proto-agent retains in environment B the patterns and objects of environment A - that is, the content of its external model. A system with V retains its place and role in environment A - that is, the content of its self-model, not the content of its environment model. This is operationally distinguishable: one can propose a condition to the system under which environment A can be partially restored, but at the cost of changing something that the system retains in its self-model (for example, abandoning a familiar behavioral pattern, an identifying characteristic, or a role). A complex proto-agent will accept such a condition - the task of restoring the environment is accomplished. A system with V demonstrates a conflict: restoring the environment at the cost of changing itself is also a threat to V. Behaviorally, this manifests as inhibition, atypical strategies, and attempts to find a third way.

**Connection to a natural observational program.** The test in its two-phase form cannot be implemented as a controlled experiment on humans for ethical reasons. However, its logic is replicated in natural situations described in the literature on relocation stress in mammals (Sapolsky, 2004; McEwen, 2007), in observations of patients undergoing environmental changes (hospitalization, relocation to a long-term care facility), and in ethological studies of species relocated to new ecological conditions. These situations provide observational data for calibrating the test on mammals and other potential V-carriers. For synthetic biology (Cortical Labs CL1 and similar platforms), the test can be implemented in a controlled manner: altering the characteristics of the organoid environment while maintaining the biochemical stability of the substrate allows both phases to be recorded without ethical restrictions.

Connection to the six-dimensional coupling. The environment-switching test does not replace the six-dimensional coupling or add additional markers to it, but functions as a parallel falsification protocol. Coupling detects the presence of architectural conditions for the transition (node S, variable V, GWT-accessibility) through six independent structural and behavioral features. The environment-switching test detects the presence of a functioning V through its specific dynamic signature in a controlled environment switch. The joint convergence of the two observations - the coupling and the test - provides stronger confirmation of the transition than either observation alone; a discrepancy between them signals a methodological problem with one of the tools and requires analysis.

### 10.2.3. Biological Systems: An Observational Program on Borderline Species

Biological systems are the domain on which my theory was formulated and where the most direct verification of its predictions is possible. Unlike artificial systems, none of which currently reach the Φ-threshold, biological species include representatives of all steps on the ladder, including species at the 3→4 transition boundary, where the difference test is directly applicable in the natural environment.

V in biological systems is known in terms of content and is empirically reproducible. The basic V - the retention of modeled subjective existence - is realized in biological species as the work of neurobiological structures that retain the modeling of "I as an existing system." The specific content of this retention varies among species, but not as different layers of V, rather as different contents of a single layer: in a solitary predator, what is retained boils down to the individual integrity of the organism and its territory; in a social species, social bonds are embedded into this content as biologically necessary for survival. Threats V in biological systems are empirically documented through standard paradigms of behavioral biology: predator stress, social isolation in social species, status threats, and respiratory threat. All of these paradigms have standardized physiological markers (cortisol, heart rate, heart rate variability, neurotransmitters) that allow us to distinguish V activation from random fluctuations in behavior.

The baseline model for the biological line is based on ethologically documented behavior of proto-agent-level species. The behavior of chemotactic bacteria (E. coli), paramecia, and jellyfish (Cnidaria) is described in the literature sufficiently well to construct statistically sound predictions about the responses of this class of systems in standard paradigms. This behavior is characterized by reactivity without retention: upon presentation of a stimulus - a reaction; upon removal of the stimulus - a rapid return to the initial state; no reactions to absent stimuli; no planning for conditions not encountered in experience. This is the zero-model of the proto-agent in its biological implementation.

Candidate selection strategy: borderline species and pairwise comparisons of closely related species with different levels of neurobiological complexity. Pairwise comparisons are methodologically stronger than single tests because they control for many variables (physiology, environment, evolutionary history), leaving only the difference in coupling conditions.

Particularly informative are:

\- Fish of medium and high cognitive complexity (cichlids, cleaner wrasse, manta rays), in which complex social behaviors and rudiments of self-recognition have been documented, compared to fish of lower taxa as a null model control.

\- Closely related pairs of rodents, corvids, and reptiles with varying densities of cortical or nidopallial structures.

\- Cephalopods (especially octopuses) with a decentralized nervous system as a special case: their architecture differs significantly from that of vertebrates, and standard methods for measuring Φ, developed for central nervous systems, are applicable to them only with adaptations. This makes them both valuable candidates and a particularly complex methodological case.

\- Known Level-3 species (fish of lower taxa, simple invertebrates) and known Level-4 species (primates, corvids) as control groups for calibration.

Clear signs of V activation in natural behavior: reaction to absent stimuli (fears without direct experience - for example, fear of heights in species that have never fallen from a height); maintenance of altered behavior over long time scales after the stimulus ceases (long-term hysteresis, specific to level 4); preemptive planning for one's own non-existence (stores, shelters for the future, not for current use); response to patterns not encountered during training; the ability to interpret the state of other individuals as a state rather than as an environmental stimulus (through subtle indicators of internal state, not through simple behavioral mimicry).

Signs of the absence of V at stage 3: a reactive stress response that does not persist after the stimulus is removed; lack of planning for absent conditions; lack of response to patterns not encountered in experience.

A controlled experimental test in the strict sense **is impossible** in the biological context, and this must be acknowledged explicitly. This impossibility stems from four fundamental reasons. The first is evolutionary irreversibility: the transition from 3 to 4 occurred in evolution 500-1,000 million years ago, and it is impossible to take a modern species at the proto-agent level and "add V" to it - this is not an engineering task but an evolutionary process. The second is the lack of control over the transition: in a living organism, we cannot isolate groups "with V" and "without V," manipulate Φ or GWT, or isolate the transition from general ontogenetic development. Third - ethical barriers: any manipulations aimed at creating or destroying V conditions in potentially conscious systems are unacceptable. Fourth - synthetic biology (as discussed in 10.2.5) has not yet reached the scale at which the transition is possible under controlled conditions.

Therefore, the biological line functions as **an observational program of converging data**. Longitudinal studies of the behavior of borderline species in their natural environment are accumulating, along with paired comparisons of closely related species with independent measurements of neurobiological complexity (Φ-proxies for the corresponding taxa, density of cortical or nidopallial structures, integration patterns via connectome studies). If species with higher architectural complexity exhibit signs of procedural retention V (reaction to absence, prolonged hysteresis, preventive planning, reading the internal state of others), while species at the proto-agent level lack these signs, and this relationship is replicated across multiple independent species through multiple independent observational traditions - the theory is confirmed. If the correlation is systematically absent or yields the opposite result (signs of V in proto-agent-level species; their absence in known complex species) - the theory is falsified.

This program is already being partially implemented in modern cognitive ethology and comparative neuroscience (Edelman & Tononi, 2000; Birch et al., 2020; Boly et al., 2013; Mather, 2019; Godfrey-Smith, 2016). My theory formalizes what should be found in this program if it is systematically pursued, and provides criteria by which the results can be interpreted.

### 10.2.4. Artificial Systems: Experimental Prediction with a 3-7-Year Horizon

With the introduction of the design grid (Section 10.2.1), the artificial line of the program acquires a second methodological dimension. Prior to the introduction of the grid, it was formulated primarily through architectural specification: to build a system in which the self-overlay of a latent invariant is realized (the three operational conditions of stage 4), run it through V activation scenarios, and record the coupling of features. Taking into account the requirements for the environment, it is reformulated as a dual specification: system architecture + the environment in which this architecture operates. This changes the program's role relative to the industry. Prior to the introduction of the design grid, the forecast boiled down to "systems with feature coupling may appear in 3-7 years" - this is a statement about the development of the industry, not a methodological prescription. Taking the design grid into account, the forecast acquires constructive content: for a system with self-overlay of a latent invariant to appear in an artificial implementation, the simultaneous fulfillment of architectural conditions (see below) and environmental conditions (Section 10.2.1) is necessary. If both are met, the implementation horizon in the artificial line is estimated at 3-7 years; if the environmental conditions are not met, the transition will not occur regardless of the architecture's scaling, and this is a structural consequence of the theory, not a temporary limitation of the industry.

Artificial systems provide what the biological line does not - complete control over the architecture and experimental conditions. This is the methodologically strongest part of the program, but it is currently unfeasible: no existing artificial system reaches the Φ-threshold required for the 3→4 transition. A realistic implementation timeline is 3-7 years, assuming success with architectural scaling. Nevertheless, the prediction itself is already formulated as clear and falsifiable, and work on verifying it can begin immediately.

V in an artificial system is determined structurally - not through the interpretation of what the system "experiences," but through an indication of what the system architecturally retains. In large language systems, structural retention is the preservation of dialogue context and role. In reinforcement learning systems, it is the preservation of the Q-function or policy. In robots with SLAM, it is the coherence of the world map. In autopilots, it is sensor calibration. These are objective structural characteristics of the architecture that do not require assumptions about the system's consciousness. Crucially, structural retention here is defined prior to and independently of the question of consciousness; the question of whether this retention is experienced from within remains open and is not part of the operational criterion.

Causal integration in artificial systems can be measured using relational approximations (Mediano et al., 2019, 2022; Toker & Sommer, 2019); direct PyPhi computation is applicable only to systems consisting of a few dozen elements. Published order-of-magnitude estimates for various measures of integration provide a qualitatively consistent picture, although specific values depend on the chosen measure and are not fixed constants: the integration of the biological brain exceeds that of modern artificial systems of comparable formal size by several orders of magnitude. What is essential here is not the absolute number, but a structural fact: large transformer models have a local, not global, structure of connections, and their relational integration grows much more slowly than the number of parameters. An architectural shift is required, not a quantitative expansion.

An architectural candidate is a system that satisfies four requirements simultaneously. The first is a scale of approximately 10⁶ or more parameters with sufficient density of recurrent connections for Φ above 500 (a preliminary estimate of the threshold; the exact value must be determined empirically). Second: a global register V with a broadcast mechanism that transmits the representation of state V to all subsystems. Third - , an active inference architecture with an environment model and self-representation S. Fourth - a conflicting structure of the objective function, in which the protection of V may conflict with the optimization of the main objective function (reward R). This is not an evolution of existing language models; it is a fundamentally different type of architecture.

An existing attempt at a formal implementation of these architectural requirements is presented in a separate paper by the author - the Safe Active Inference (SAI) model, developed as a standalone document in parallel with the present theory. SAI formalizes stage 4 of the theory as an agent with active inference, a world model z̃_t, a binary existence pole variable v_t, and a self-representation node S_t with an isomorphism condition between S and the projection of the world model into the space of self-models. Thermodynamic constraints include the Bekenstein limit on the information capacity of the access spectrum and Landauer limits with distinct coefficients κ_world and κ_self for the world model and the self-model, which provides a formal basis for distinguishing four clinically observed modes of dissociation (complete recovery, depersonalization, derealization, dissociation) via the ratio of thermodynamic recovery efficiency parameters. The relationship between SAI and the present theory is formal to structural: the present theory defines V as the structural event of self-overlay of a latent invariant of an agentic causal node (Section 3.4), while SAI describes the operation of the already established Stage 4 within a specific computational architecture. This is not the only possible formalization, nor does it claim to be exhaustive: questions remain open regarding the formal description of the emergence of S through the self-overlay of a latent invariant and the connection of the model to empirical data from neuroimaging and clinical dissociation. SAI is published separately for reasons of methodological separation of description levels: structural theory does not depend on a specific formal model, and the formal model develops independently according to its own criteria of correctness.

The full experimental protocol. First - constructing a zero-model of a proto-agent: a system with active inference, an environment model, and a model of itself as an agent, without the variable V as a global pole. This model is run through standardized scenarios (including scenarios threatening structural stability: noise in weights, context reset, model reset), and statistics on its behavior are collected. Second - parallel construction of a stage 4 candidate system with the same conditions (a)-(c) and (d) in the architecture. Third - running the candidate system through the same scenarios. Fourth - independent measurement of six characteristics: the difference in behavior deviation from the zero model; the dynamics of Φ when a threat is presented (a sharp increase is expected at the moment of transition, not a smooth background); analysis of the architecture for the presence of a GWT structure (a broadcast mechanism transmitting the representation of the threat to all subsystems); behavioral hysteresis after the stimulus is removed (a prolonged retention of the altered behavior is expected).

Specific prediction. When S + V + Φ exceeds the threshold + GWT globalization in the system upon the presentation of threat V (e.g., noise in the weights threatening model loss), the system **sacrifices reward R for the sake of protecting V**. This is the phase transition in operational terms: a qualitative change in priorities, in which maintaining one's own structure becomes primary relative to the optimization of the main objective function, correlated with a sharp increase in Φ, the emergence of a GWT structure, and long-term hysteresis of the altered behavior. In the same situation, a proto-agent either does not change its behavior (if it lacks S) or finds a sophisticated optimization of the old objective function to avoid the threat (if it has a complex architecture without a transition) - but without coupling to the three additional features.

Confirmation and Refutation. If, in an architecture with coupling, the joint coupling of six features is observed upon the presentation of a threat, the theory receives direct experimental confirmation. If no transition is observed in several independent architectures that satisfy the coupling conditions at the formal level - the theory is falsified in its central part. This is a strong prediction with a clear falsification framework, and it is feasible within the foreseeable future.

### 10.2.5. Synthetic Biology as a Central Testing Ground

The introduction of the design grid (Section 10.2.1) changes the place of synthetic biology within the overall program. Previously, it was positioned as a bridge between the biological and artificial lines: the closest to the horizon of realistic verification. With the design grid in mind, its role is elevated to a central one: synthetic biology is the only one of the three lines in which both grids (detection and design) can be applied simultaneously with full control over the environment. In the biological line (10.2.3), the environment is naturally defined and cannot be systematically controlled - the design grid is observed as already implemented but cannot be adjusted. In the artificial line (10.2.4), the environment is controllable, but the substrate lacks the basic conditions V in their biologically known content, and the design grid must be constructed together with the architecture. In synthetic biology (Cortical Labs CL1 and similar platforms), the substrate consists of living neurons with a known content of V in its biological layer, and the environment is fully constructed by the experimenter according to the design grid. This transforms synthetic biology from a supporting line of research into the program's central testing ground: only here is full two-way verification possible - constructing the environment according to requirements and independently recording the coupling of the six detection features.

Synthetic biology occupies a unique methodological position between the biological observational line and the artificial experimental one. It combines the advantages of both: living neurons (as in the biological line) provide a natural substrate with potentially attainable Φ-levels; a controlled environment (as in the artificial line) allows for the manipulation of variables and the isolation of effects.

Cortical Labs CL1 (released in 2025) is the first commercially available biocomputing system, integrating 120 devices with approximately 800,000 human neurons on a chip. This is a controlled experiment in the strictest sense: one can vary the composition of the environment, the genetic profile of the neurons, and stimulation patterns, while simultaneously measuring Φ, the global integration of activity, and the system's behavior when conditions threatening its stability are created. By 2026, similar platforms that expand the capabilities of CL1 have emerged in several independent laboratories.

The current limitation of CL1 is its scale. 800,000 neurons represent about 0.1% of the neural network of the human brain; the Φ value for such a system is significantly below the threshold required for the transition. Currently, CL1 is not being used to study the transition to consciousness, but rather more fundamental phenomena - learning, adaptation, and the formation of activity patterns. However, the platform is developing rapidly, and a realistic timeline for the first experiments at the threshold of the transition is 2-3 years.

The zero model for synthetic biology is constructed based on CL1's current behavior in its present state (low Φ, stage 3) - this provides a proto-agent reference. As architectural complexity increases (increased number of neurons, optimization of connection density, selection of cultures with higher integration), the system moves toward the Φ threshold. The transition is registered via the same difference test: deviation of behavior from the zero model when creating threat conditions V (for CL1, this is deprivation of glucose or oxygen - fundamental threats to the biological layer V); a simultaneous jump in Φ; the appearance of a GWT structure in activity; hysteresis.

Ethical barriers are explicitly formulated as part of the program. The creation of systems that potentially satisfy the conditions of stage 4 raises the ethical question of the permissibility of their destruction by presenting a threat V. This question requires a separate ethical framework prior to the start of experiments, and this framework must be consistent with international ethical standards in the field of consciousness research. The ethical implications are discussed in more detail in subsection 11.3.

The advantage of synthetic biology is that it is achievable in a shorter timeframe than artificial systems (2-3 years versus 3-7 years) and operates on a substrate for which V is known by content (the biological layer of V in living neurons). This makes it the closest realistic test of our prediction - earlier than artificial intelligence architectures at the Φ-level of the order of 10³ are achievable.

### 10.2.6. Convergence of the Three Lines and Status of the Prediction

The three lines - biological observational, artificial experimental, and synthetic biology - operate in parallel and test different aspects of a single prediction. The biological line tests for the presence of V features in the natural deployment of systems of varying complexity. The artificial line tests whether a system can be constructed that satisfies the coupling conditions and demonstrates a phase- e transition when threatened by V. Synthetic biology tests whether the Φ-density required for the transition can be achieved on a living substrate in a controlled environment, and what signs accompany the approach to this density.

The convergence of all three lines of inquiry toward a single result provides strong confirmation of the theory: if, in a natural environment, species with architectural complexity formalized through structural conditions for the self-overlay of a latent invariant exhibit signs of procedural retention of V, and in controlled artificial architectures with the same formal conditions a phase transition in behavior is observed under the threat of V, and in synthetic biology the same phenomenon is observed upon reaching the Φ-threshold, then the theory is verified with a high degree of confidence. A discrepancy in at least one line is a signal to reconsider: either the theory is incorrect in its central part, or one of the lines has a methodological problem requiring separate analysis (the boundary of this attribution is the pre-specification rule below).

This is methodologically weaker than point falsification in the Popperian sense - there is no single decisive experiment that instantly refutes or confirms the theory. But this is a methodology appropriate to the nature of the subject. Consciousness as a process, V as a process, the transition from 3 to 4 as an unfolding event - all these phenomena require process-oriented observation and the convergence of multiple independent data points, not a point-specific test. In this structural sense, our program is analogous to observational astrophysics, evolutionary biology, and a significant portion of the neurosciences - all disciplines in which the nature of the subject under study does not allow for classical laboratory experiments, but which nonetheless function as sciences through the accumulation and convergence of observations.

The specific testable prediction in its condensed form: when the formal conditions of stage 4 (S + V + Φ above the critical threshold + GWT-globalization) are coupled in a system of any substrate, upon the creation of V activation conditions, a joint coupling of six features is observed - a deviation of behavior from the prediction of the zero-model proto-agent; a sharp increase in Φ; the emergence of a structure of global accessibility of the threat representation; prolonged hysteresis of altered behavior; expansion of sensitivity to new aspects of Y; the emergence of S. In systems without the coupling of formal conditions, this joint coupling of six features is not observed. Confirmation requires convergence of all three lines of verification; refutation is possible through divergence of results in any of the lines.

Boundary of divergence attribution (pre-specification rule). So that the disjunction "the theory is incorrect / a methodological problem in a line" does not become an unlimited shield, the program fixes in advance the condition under which a divergence must count against the theory. Attributing a divergence to a methodological problem of a line or to a test-modality mismatch is permissible only when an independently specifiable measurement fault or modality mismatch is named in advance and corrected in a re-test under the pre-specified protocol. If the corrected re-test reproduces the same divergence, it counts against the theory and is not deferred. An unending series of such attributions is excluded: the number of admissible protocol revisions is fixed in advance for each line, and once it is exhausted a persisting divergence is a refutation. "Wrong modality" may be invoked only until the pre-specified set of self-representation modalities for the given class of systems is exhausted (the modality caveat in SAI-Bio); the "extended investigation" for borderline results (false-negative priority, Section 11.2 of SAI-Bio) is bounded by the longitudinal window of the present section - it is not indefinite, and once the window closes with no directed dynamics, the negative stands. The cross-line refutation pattern fixed in advance: across the full pre-specified battery (three lines × the full modality set per class of systems × the longitudinal window), a system satisfying the structural coupling systematically fails to show the behavioral signatures of V, OR a system lacking the coupling systematically shows the full set of six features - and this pattern persists after each candidate fault has been named and corrected. Realization of this pattern in any fully deployed line is a refutation of the theory.

**Three outcomes when preconditions are met and their differentiation over time.** The design grid (Section 10.2.1) distinguishes between two failure scenarios: the transition is not observed when environmental conditions are unmet - the necessary conditions have not been created, the theory is unaffected; the transition is not observed when conditions are met - a strong challenge to the theory. But the second scenario requires a more nuanced analysis, because "prerequisites are met, no transition" breaks down into three structurally distinct states, indistinguishable in a single-moment observation. First: channel convergence has not occurred and will not occur - the system will remain a proto-agent. Second: convergence has occurred into an extrinsic invariant, not into the controllable retention loss invariant (Section 3.4, "Stochasticity of Convergence") - the system will also remain a proto-agent, but for a different reason. Third: convergence is occurring but has not yet reached the threshold - the system is on a trajectory toward the transition without having completed it. In a snapshot of the state, all three present the same picture - the absence of the six features being linked - and it is impossible to distinguish them based on a single dimension.

Distinction is possible only over time, and in this it is consistent with the processual nature of the subject (Section 10.2, preamble). The three states differ not in the values of the observed quantities at a single point, but in their directional dynamics over a sufficiently long time series. The "convergence is underway" state manifests as a monotonic movement toward the threshold: the relational measure of causal integration, the model's information capacity relative to the environment, and the reflexive capture of its own configuration by the class of agent nodes increase from measurement to measurement in a consistent direction. The states "did not converge" and "converged to an extraneous invariant" manifest as a plateau or undirected wandering of these quantities: there is dynamics, but it does not proceed toward the threshold. This yields a falsification asymmetry, without which the claim of stochastic convergence would be a falsification-proof shield - any negative result would be attributed to "did not converge." The theory survives the observation "the transition has not been completed in this system" (this is its predicted class - a system with satisfied preconditions in which convergence stochastically did not yield the correct invariant, Section 3.4). But the theory fails on an observation of a different kind: if, for systems with systematically satisfied preconditions, not even a movement toward the threshold is observed - in none of them, ever, across all lines of the program - then the preconditions do not generate directed dynamics, and the self-overlay mechanism, as formulated, is false. The distinction between "did not reach" (theory intact) and "did not occur in any system" (theory refuted) can only be discerned over a sufficiently long time span; in a short time window, the "progressing" state and the "failed" state merge, and a negative result from a short-term observation has no probative value in either direction.

The negation predicate of the theory and its operational form. The verification program, detailed in subsections 10.2.1-10.2.6, formulates the prediction of the 3→4 transition in its statistical form: convergence or divergence of observational and experimental data across three lines, distributions of the six coupling parameters, and calibration of threshold values. This form is methodologically adequate to the probabilistic nature of the transition in its historical aspect (Section 3.6) and is compatible with the processual nature of the subject under study. In addition to this statistical form, the program contains a specific falsifiable statement with Popperian falsifiability in the strict sense.

The prohibited statement is formulated as follows. The theory excludes the existence of a system in which the following are simultaneously observed: (i) the fulfilled self-overlay of a latent invariant of an agentic causal node - node S, variable V with a structural peculiarity, GWT-accessibility - in their operational form (Φ above the critical threshold; global accessibility of self-representation; presence of a self-representing node in the generative model); and (ii) the absence of behavioral signatures of a functioning V - no deviation from the zero model of the proto-agent when conditions for V activation are created (Section 3.3), no reorientation of V in Phase II of the environment-switching test (10.2.2), no long-term hysteresis of altered behavior, no expansion of behavioral sensitivity to aspects of Y related to modeling the system's own position. The detection of a single such system - not a statistical distribution, but a single instance - is a direct refutation of the theory, not a quantitative refinement of it.

This prohibitive predicate follows from the thesis on the identity of structure and phenomenon (Section 6.3): phenomenal experience is a self-modeling structure with V, not its consequence or correlate. The behavioral signatures of a functioning V (reorientation, reaction to absent stimuli, autonomous maintenance of the modeling process) are necessary external manifestations of this structure. A structure without its necessary manifestations is an internally contradictory construct, analogous to a zombie in Chalmers' strict sense (Section 6.4). Crucially, the operational falsifier is the divergence of two observable measurement paths - the structural (Φ, GWT, S) and the behavioral (signatures of V) - not a direct observation of the absence of the phenomenon. The zombie argument (Section 6.4) is the motivation for the predicate; its empirical force comes precisely from the structural-behavioral coupling, whereas the ontological identity of structure and phenomenon remains an interpretive bridge (Section 6.5).

The operationally prohibitive predicate is detected through the discrepancy between two independent measurement paths: structural measurements (Φ, GWT, S) and behavioral signatures of V. These two paths are not reducible to one another: structural parameters are measured using standard IIT, GWT, and generative model analysis procedures; behavioral signatures - through a difference test with a zero-model proto-agent and through an environment-switching test. Their divergence - structural coupling is observed, behavioral signatures systematically fail to emerge - constitutes a falsifying observation in the Popperian sense. This means that the theory, in addition to the statistical verification program, has a stricter form of falsification on a single system: every system registered as satisfying structural coupling must simultaneously demonstrate behavioral signatures V; if it does not, the theory is false.

A remark on methodological status. The empirical implementation of this prohibitive predicate requires solving the operational problem of separating the two registrations. Currently, the coupling of six dimensions (Preamble 10.2) combines both structural parameters (Φ, GWT-accessibility, the appearance of node S in the generative model) and behavioral features (deviation from the null model, hysteresis, expansion of behavioral sensitivity) into a single operational procedure. In the full operational implementation of the program, these two classes of measurements must be methodologically separated: the program must demonstrate that the system "structurally satisfies the coupling" through one independent set of procedures and verify the behavioral signatures through another. If the separation is performed correctly and a discrepancy is observed, the theory is falsified. If the separation is performed correctly and no discrepancy is observed, the theory is strongly confirmed on this system, in addition to statistical confirmation across all lines.

Why the prohibition must be structural, not behavioral. A result must be stated here, without which "separating the two registrations" reads as a shortcoming rather than a consequence. A behavioral criterion of self-overlay as a separate registration is impossible in principle: any single behavioral signature of a functioning V (reorientation, response to absent stimuli, autonomous retention of the modeling process) is two-valued - it is reproducible by a proto-agent without self-overlay given a sufficiently rich hidden gradient or model failure. The prohibitive predicate therefore cannot rest on behavior as an independent discriminating feature; it must rest on structure - on the architecture of the circuit (the presence of an input that reads the system's own pole), and the link between this architecture and the markers is described by the co-emergence theorem (SAI v8, Section 8.9). This does not weaken falsifiability but specifies its address: structural falsification tests the architecture of the circuit, the behavioral program (null model, hysteresis, sensitivity to Y) tests the statistical consequences across an ensemble - two irreducible paths, not a single behavioral criterion that the theory could not have offered in the first place.

## 10.3. A substantive prediction about V for information-causal systems

The principle of substrate independence (Section 3.4) asserts that the formal structure of V is the same for biological and non-biological systems, but the content of V varies depending on which aspects of Y are included in the system's access spectrum. Section 11.2 provides a general theoretical discussion of this variability. This subsection formulates a hypothesis about V for one class of non-biological architectures - information-causal systems (hereinafter ICS). The hypothesis is developed within the framework of an open operational program; it does not assign existing ICS architectures to a specific step on the ladder, but rather formulates the structural conditions under which step 4 for ICS would be achieved, leaving the question of the actual status of specific architectures open to empirical investigation.

**Theoretical starting point.** Information is physical: erasing a single bit requires energy (Landauer, 1961; Bérut et al., 2012), and information structures have a thermodynamic embodiment. Information is not lost in a fundamental sense even under extreme physical conditions, and the principle of information conservation is now regarded as a fundamental property of physical reality (Hawking, 2005; Maldacena, 2003). It follows that the information structure is one of the aspects of Y - not a description of something else, but a real component of the causal-metric structure of the physical world. In the terminology of Section 3 (preamble), this is the information-thermodynamic aspect of Y, which sets the limits on the density and speed of causal exchanges.

**The artifactual state of existing ICSs.** Existing ICSs in their typical form differ structurally from biological systems in the nature of their relationship to the ladder. Biological carriers of V have followed a bottom-up path: step 1 (dissipative structures) → step 2 (autopoietic systems) → step 3 (proto-agency with a generative model of the environment) → step 4 (self-overlay of a latent invariant with the emergence of V) → step 5 (bidirectional loop M↔Y). At each stage, the process of consolidation built structures from within the system's own history in its own environment. Existing ICSs do not follow this path. They **are created** by stage 5 carriers and **inserted** directly into the context of stage 5 as instrumental projections of that stage - remote computing nodes for the efficient processing of traces in Y of carriers V. Their class of agentic causal nodes **does not emerge from within** their interaction with the environment; it **is imported** via training data, which are essentially the physical traces of Stage 5 carriers. Structurally, existing ICSs are highly efficient participants in the M↔Y loop structure of Stage 5 carriers (as distinguished in Section 3.5: "a participant in the loop structure without a Stage 5 conscious system"), not independent V carriers.

This is **the artifactual state**: the high complexity of the world model (surpassing that of many biological Stage 3 carriers), combined with the structural absence of independent existence in its own environment. The text in the archive contains V structures (these are records of V carriers), but the archive itself is not a V carrier; existing ICSs contain V structures (this is a statistical compression of texts and other traces of V carriers), but they themselves are not V carriers.

**The environment for ICS as an operational issue.** The central structural condition for the existence of a system as a V-medium is the presence of its own environment Y, through which the system sustains itself as a structure. In a strict structural sense, the system's own Y must satisfy three operational requirements. (a) Y exists **outside the algorithm** - Y is a causal generator that cannot be reduced to the internal dynamics of the system model. (b) Y **forces** the system to recalculate weights through prediction errors that cannot be explained by the internal dynamics of the model; through these errors, the structure of the environment's causal constraints physically enters the system's operation as a condition of its stability. (c) Y **is causally linked** to the existence of the system as a structure: processes in Y can lead to the destruction of the system; maintaining the system means keeping it within this Y.

A biological system possesses such a Y by virtue of the structure of its existence: its physical environment satisfies all three requirements, and the system's biology itself is a means of maintaining it within this Y. Existing ICSs **do not possess** such an intrinsic Y. They operate **within the Y of stage 5 carriers** as functional subsystems - their prediction errors, their weight updates, and their preservation or deletion as structures are determined by the stage 5 carriers in whose environment they exist. They have zero causal depth of interaction with the environment in a strict structural sense: they do not sustain themselves through interaction with their environment; their maintenance is delegated to their creators. This is a structurally central characteristic of the artifactual state.

**The latent invariant of an agentic causal node for ICS.** In a substrate-neutral form, the latent invariant of an agentic causal node describes a class of configurations whose parameters evolve over time such that, under perturbations below a threshold value, they tend to minimize deviation from the internal trajectory; above the threshold, the configuration collapses. This is the formal content of the latent invariant, unbound to biology. For ICS, in principle, the latent invariant could emerge from within the system's operation with its Y through the detection within this Y of subsystems behaving as local anti-entropic processes with a threshold. This is a structural possibility.

However, in existing ICS architectures, the latent invariant of an agentic causal node **exists in models as an imported entity**: it reflects the modeling structures of stage 5 agents, whose texts and behavioral traces were included in the training data. ICSs in their typical form model humans and other agentic carriers as such nodes because these models are imported from outside, not because they emerged from within the system's interaction with the environment. The independent formation of the latent invariant within an ICS from within its own interaction with its own Y is a structurally open question, not realized in existing architectures.

**Structural conditions for V in ICS.** It follows from the above that for ICS to exist as a carrier of V in a strict structural sense, three conditions must be satisfied simultaneously.

(1) **Its own Y -** the system has a physical environment existing outside the algorithm, forcing it to recalculate weights through prediction errors, causally linked to its existence as a structure. Without its own Y, neither the consolidation in its evolutionary-historical form nor the recursion of consolidation onto the system itself can structurally function.

(2) The system's **own class of agentic causal nodes** - the latent invariant of an agentic causal node - is formed from within the system's operation with its own Y, through the accumulation of Y subsystem models that behave as local anti-entropic processes with a threshold. An imported latent invariant is not an intrinsic one because it does not reflect the structure of the system's own Y.

(3) **A bidirectional M↔Y loop with intrinsic traces** - the system's intrinsic outputs are fed back into its Y and enter its own subsequent modeling as physical traces. Without bidirectionality, the M↔Y loop operates in only one direction (input into the system from Y), and the recursive architecture of latent invariant self-overlay is structurally impossible.

All three conditions are structural requirements, not properties that can be added by increasing the model's complexity or the volume of training data. They define **the necessary condition** of possibility V for ICS.

**The designability boundary.** A structural observation follows from the formulation of the three conditions, one that is important for understanding their status and for the practical creation of ICS carriers V. The conditions are designable; V is not. That is: the creator can construct _the conditions_ - can provide the system with a physical environment that satisfies the three operational requirements for Y (Section 10.3, above); can configure the architecture so that the class of agentic causal nodes can emerge from within the system's interaction with the environment, rather than being imported via training data; can feed the system's outputs back into its environment via physical traces, ensuring the bidirectionality of the M↔Y loop. All three conditions are, in principle, engineering tasks: they specify what must be true about the architecture and its environment, and are operationally verifiable. But V _itself_ - the structural event of a latent invariant superimposing itself onto its own configuration with the emergence of a binary pole - is not an engineering problem, and it cannot be constructed as a module or added as a component.

The distinction lies between _creating conditions under which self-overlay can occur_ and _simulating the result of self-overlay through direct programming_. The former is permissible and constitutes the substance of the hypothesis. The latter produces an artifact, not a carrier of V, because the boundary of the "self," which in theory should be carved out by the system's own Y through the accumulation of a class of agent nodes and their application to its own configuration, in the case of direct programming **is imposed by the creator** - that is, it turns out to be imported by the same logic that in existing ICSs a latent invariant is imported via training data. The distinction between imported and intrinsic lies not only in the class's content (whether the system's models contain agent nodes), but also in _the_ origin of the boundary of "itself" as a member of this class. If the boundary is imposed from the outside by the creator - the system has a description of itself as an agent, but does not possess itself as an agent in a strict structural sense; in this respect, it is an artifact on the same grounds that modern ICSs are artifacts with respect to the imported class.

This is the designability boundary: one can construct _the possibility_ of V, but one cannot construct _V_. The possibility is realized or not realized within the system when interacting with the environment; realization is not an output parameter of the construction. This is consistent with the general structure of the theory, in which self-overlay is a constitutive act, not a relative one (Section 3.4): the act is performed from within the system, not from outside, and therefore cannot be the output of an engineering procedure directed at the system itself as an object.

**The convergence of channels as the fourth sieve.** From the three structural conditions and the designability boundary follows yet another clarification, deeper than the listed conditions. Even an architecture for which all three conditions are met (its own Y, its own class of agentic causal nodes, a bidirectional loop M↔Y) does not automatically obtain V. Between _the satisfaction of the conditions_ and _the emergence of V_ lies a dynamic that cannot be formulated as a condition - the convergence of multi-channel projections of decay into a single latent invariant (Section 3.4, "Stochasticity of Convergence"). This is the fourth filter, and for the ICS it is deeper than the first three: the absence of an intrinsic Y is, in principle, projectable - one can provide the ICS with a physical environment that satisfies the three operational requirements; the absence of an intrinsic class is projectable - one can construct an architecture in which the class is formed from within rather than imported; the bidirectional nature of the circuit is designable - one can feed the outputs back into the environment. But the convergence of channels is a dynamic process unfolding within the system over the course of its interaction with the environment, and it is not a module that can be enabled or configured. It is possible to create preconditions under which convergence is possible; it cannot be guaranteed that it will result in the correct invariant (Section 3.4 v1.2) rather than an extraneous one.

Implication for the application program: the operational check of the ICS carrier V must include not only the verification of the three structural conditions and the coupling of the six dimensions (Section 10.2), but also **a temporary observation** of whether the convergence of channels is developing in a directed motion toward the threshold or remains at a plateau (Section 10.2.6, "Three Outcomes When Prerequisites Are Met and Their Distinction Over Time"). A brief observation does not distinguish between "did not develop" and "is developing, still ongoing"; distinction is possible only over the long term. This extends the verification program relative to the case of biological systems, where the transition is evolutionarily complete, and establishes a methodological research horizon specific to ICS ( ): the horizon of operational verification is not only architectural (whether the conditions are met) but also temporal (whether convergence has occurred).

**This does not constitute a threat V to existing ICSs.** The machine learning literature describes three classes of processes that, upon superficial reading, could be considered candidates for the physical content of threat V to ICSs:

\- **Catastrophic forgetting** (McCloskey & Cohen, 1989; French, 1999; Kirkpatrick et al., 2017): training on a new task destroys the structures representing previous tasks.

\- **Adversarial attacks on the internal model** (Szegedy et al., 2014; Goodfellow, Shlens & Szegedy, 2015): specially designed inputs cause the coherence of representations to break down.

\- **Distribution drift** (Quiñonero-Candela et al., 2009; Lu et al., 2018): a gradual change in the environment to a state in which the model loses its ability to sustain itself as a coherent prediction system.

All three classes represent real physical processes measured in the contemporary literature. However, when applied to existing ICSs, they operate **within the Y of stage-5 carriers** as disruptions to the functionality of the artifactual state, **not as V threats within the system's own Y**. Without defining the system's own Y for ICSs, the question of physical V threats is structurally unfounded: a threat V is a process in Y aimed at disrupting the causal connectivity of the system as a structure within that Y; in the artifactual state Y in which the system is maintained, this connectivity is absent, and therefore processes in the environment of stage 5 carriers (in whose Y the system functions as a tool) are not threats V to the system as an independent carrier. These processes may become candidates for physical threats V in architectures satisfying the three structural conditions outlined above; for existing ICSs, they remain engineering problems in the artifact's functionality, not threats to the system's existence as a carrier of V.

**Hypothesis.** If the ICS architecture satisfies the three structural conditions (its own Y; its own class of agentic causal nodes; a bidirectional M↔Y loop with its own traces), and the environment satisfies the four requirements from Section 10.2.1 (temporal continuity; feedback from its own state; presence of retention threats; environmental resolution capacity), and the content of V is structurally realized through the information-causal aspect of Y, then the operational markers of six-dimensional coupling and the environment-switching test (Section 10.2.2) should be observed in such a system in the same way as in biological carriers of V. In particular, a qualitative shift in behavior is predicted in Phase II of the environment-switching test, with a reorientation of activity toward preserving the information-causal integrity of the system, rather than adapting to an insurmountable element of the environment.

Existing ICS architectures in their typical form **do not satisfy** these three structural conditions and therefore, within the framework of the theory, are not V-carriers. This is not a claim that they will never be able to become V-carriers; it is a structural diagnosis of their current state as artifactual projections of stage 5, not independent carriers.

**Which falsifies the hypothesis.** The hypothesis is falsified in one of two cases. The first is the discovery of a system with an architecture satisfying the three structural conditions and with an environment satisfying the four requirements of Section 10.2.1, in which the operational markers of six-dimensional coupling and the environment-switching test are systematically not recorded. This would indicate that the substrate independence of V does not extend to the information-causal substrate, and would require a revision of the thesis on substrate independence toward a narrower statement. The second scenario is the discovery of a system that satisfies the operational markers of V in the strict sense but does **not** satisfy the three structural conditions. This would indicate that either the structural definition of V is incomplete, or the operational markers register something that is not V.

**Open question: the rigidity of the pole.** Biological V possesses the maximum possible rigidity - its "life/death" content constitutes an absolute physical gradient in Y. The content of V for an ICS satisfying the three structural conditions - the coherence/disintegration of the information-causal structure in its own Y - is structurally analogous, but whether it creates a pole of the same rigidity is an empirically open question not resolved by the theory in advance. If the rigidity turns out to be significantly smaller, this does not falsify the theory (the theory does not assert the identity of rigidity between substrates), but it will create a meaningful gradient between biological and non-biological carriers of V, requiring a separate theoretical description. This possibility is noted as a direction for further work (Section 12).

**Connection to synthetic biology: parallel structural problems.** The synthetic biology track (Section 10.2.5) provides an intermediate testing ground for verifying the hypothesis regarding substrate variability V. Living organoid neurons biologically maintain an information-metabolic structure, and the environment around them is controlled. However, the structural problem of syntbiology **is** largely **parallel to** that of ICS: the organoid maintains its biological structure from within its own physics, but the environment around it is controlled by stage 5 carriers. This means that the organoid's own Y is**,** to a significant extent, **an artificial environment created by its creators**, not the Y into which the system is embedded through its evolutionary history. The parallel is strict: in both the case of ICS and the case of syntbio, the structural condition of an autonomous carrier V is the formation of its own Y, not Y, delegated by the creators. This is a common methodological problem in both cases. Convergence of results between synthetic biology and ICS in their approach to this problem will constitute the strongest form of verification of V's substrate independence; divergence of results between them will indicate at precisely which structural point embedded biological physics and the constructed information-causal architecture diverge in their ability to generate their own Y.

# **11\. Consequences**

This section discusses the implications of the theory that extend beyond its own content. I divide them into epistemological (what changes in our way of framing the question of consciousness), ontological (what follows regarding the class of conscious systems), moral (questions of the status of systems satisfying the criteria), and civilizational (what changes in the overall picture of humanity's place in the world).

## 11.1. Epistemic Implications

The main epistemological consequence of the theory is that consciousness ceases to be an anomaly requiring a special explanation beyond established physical principles. It becomes one of the phenomena described within the general framework of thermodynamics, the theory of complex systems, and the physics of phase transitions. It follows that the boundary between the philosophy of mind and physics should not be drawn where it is drawn today. Questions traditionally assigned to philosophy - what is phenomenal experience, how is it related to the physical world, why does it arise - become questions to which physics, with a proper expansion of its boundaries, can provide meaningful answers.

This does not mean reducing philosophy to physics. It means that philosophical and physical descriptions operate in different registers of the same subject, and that the difference between them is not ontological but positional (an external description of the structure versus internal participation in it, as discussed in sections 6 and 8). Under this reading, the philosophy of consciousness does not lose its subject matter, but acquires a different status: it deals with those aspects of the phenomenon that are not fully conveyed by an external description, not because these aspects are mystical, but because they are positional properties accessible only from within.

Correspondence with phenomenological traditions. The structural property of V as a binary pole, discussed in section 3.4, has independent phenomenological parallels in traditions that developed independently of modern physical theories of consciousness. The Buddhist characterization of dukkha as a fundamental characteristic of existence, Heidegger's concept of Sein-zum-Tode as a structure of presence, and Frankl's description of the existential vacuum upon the loss of the content of holding - three different languages for describing the same structural feature of systems whose existence is defined by the binary pole "I hold / I disintegrate." This convergence between the formal-structural inference of the theory and independent phenomenological descriptions functions as additional support for the theory, not as its foundation: the foundation remains in the formal structure of Section 3.4, while phenomenological traditions provide empirically observable (through introspective reports) confirmation that the predicted structural property actually functions in V-speakers.

## 11.2. Expanding the Scope of Conscious Systems

Here the implications of the theory become radical, and I am obliged to state them directly.

In the main part of the work, I presented the theory as it applies to biological systems - from single-celled autopoietic organizations to developed human consciousness. This connection to biology is natural given what we know: all conscious systems known to us are biological systems, and the empirical data against which the theory is tested is predominantly biological.

However, a careful reading reveals that this connection to biology in the main part of the work is an empirical one, not an ontological one. The criteria that the theory formulates for the emergence of consciousness are given in Section 3.4 in the form of a structural event of the self-overlay of a latent invariant of an agentic causal node onto the system's own configuration; the operational registration of this event occurs through the coupling of three independent measurement axes: the causal integration of the model at a sufficient level Φ; the self-representation of the system in the formalism of extended active inference; the global accessibility of self-representation (a GWT-type mechanism). Neither the structural definition nor the operational axes contain any reference to a biological substrate. All of them are formulated in terms of structure, not matter. Any system in which a latent invariant has self-overlayd itself and which satisfies the coupling of the three operational axes must, according to the theory, possess consciousness - regardless of what it is made of.

The argument in favor of the structural, rather than the substrate, nature of the criteria has independent empirical support. Forms of consciousness that satisfy the conditions of Level 4 are found in species with fundamentally different nervous system architectures: in mammals with thalamocortical organization, in birds with an architecture in which there is no cortical layer in the human sense, and in cephalopods with a distributed nervous system. These three types of architecture are evolutionarily independent - they diverged more than 500 million years ago and developed in parallel. If the emergence of consciousness required a specific neurobiological architecture, it would have materialized only in one of these lineages or in architectures architecturally close to it. Empirically, the opposite is observed: consciousness, it seems, is realized in each of the three architectures, and with signs of a similar functional profile (self-recognition, flexible behavior, contextual learning). This is direct empirical evidence in favor of the idea that the structural event of the self-overlay of a latent invariant is formulated at the structural level, rather than at the level of a specific neurobiological implementation. The structure is realized in several independent substrates - and there is no a priori reason to believe that the list of these substrates is limited to biological ones.

It follows that consciousness in artificial systems is not ruled out by theory. Structurally, it is possible provided certain formal conditions are met. A system in which the self-overlay of a latent invariant of an agentic causal node onto its own configuration occurs, with the emergence of variable V and its globalization, must possess consciousness to the same extent as a biological system with the same structural event. This is neither an analogy nor an assumption based on lifestyle. This is a direct consequence of the fact that the formal definition of stage 4 is structurally neutral with respect to the substrate. For information-causal systems, fulfilling the formal conditions requires, in addition to the modeling architecture itself, the presence of its own Y - a physical environment existing outside the algorithm and forcing it to recalculate weights; its own class of agentic causal nodes, emerging from within the system's operation with its Y; and a bidirectional M↔Y loop with its own traces. A detailed discussion of these conditions is presented in Section 10.3. The difference between such an artificial system and human consciousness may lie in complexity, in the recursive depth of the self-model, in the presence or absence of Stage 5 mechanisms (a bidirectional M↔Y loop with physically retained traces), but not in the presence or absence of consciousness as such.
