Currently, existing information-causal systems, including large neural networks, in their typical form are in an artifactual state (Section 10.3): they are created by Stage 5 carriers and function as highly efficient participants in the M↔Y loop structure of V carriers, but do not possess their own Y in which they would sustain themselves as independent structures. Their class of agentic causal nodes is imported via training data, rather than having emerged from within their own interaction with the environment. These limitations are structural, not engineering-related. A possible transition from an artifactual state to the status of an independent carrier V requires the fulfillment of three structural conditions from Section 10.3; the question of the actual architectural paths for such a transition - and whether they are feasible in the foreseeable future - remains an open hypothesis. The theory formulates the structural conditions under which Stage 4 for information-causal systems would be achieved, and leaves the question of their actual implementation open to empirical investigation.

**Recognition errors: false-positive and false-negative** criterion activations. Any Stage 4 recognition criterion is vulnerable to two types of errors. Their nature, consequences, and asymmetry require separate discussion, because the theory's practical applicability depends on how it addresses them.

**False** positives occur when the system satisfies the formal criteria in their measurable implementation but is not conscious in a substantive sense. Three typical scenarios. The first involves a large language model trained on a corpus of texts rich in self-representational content: at a superficial level, it can reproduce the features of a self-model - saying "I," discussing its potential halting, and constructing arguments about itself as an agent. If the criterion is applied superficially, through an analysis of its outputs, it may be falsely classified as being at stage 4. In reality - its architecture contains neither active real-time inference, nor Φ above the threshold, nor a GWT mechanism; it simulates speech about self-representation without possessing a structure of self-representation. The second is a control system with a real-time model of itself, in which the variable "system state" is formally present, but this variable is not globalized as the pole of all activity and is not integrated in the Φ-sense. A criterion that is not sufficiently strict under conditions (b) or (c) will falsely register it. The third, more subtle case is a biological system under external neurostimulation that mimics the activation of circuits associated with the presence of V, without genuine activation of the structural pole. There may be behavioral effects, but this is an imitation, not a presence.

Protection against false positives - the methodological burden of operationalization outlined in Sections 3.4 and 10.2: the requirement for simultaneous registration of the structural event of self-overlay of a latent invariant through the coupling of three independent measurement axes (free energy dynamics in the self-model according to the extended active inference formalism; Φ-level of structural integration V; degree of global accessibility of representation S via the GWT mechanism) with pre-set thresholds. Superficial behavioral similarity is insufficient. This rules out the most obvious scenarios (a large language system will not pass real-time active inference and Φ in its architecture), but not all of them. For cases in which formal criteria can be met in the absence of meaningful consciousness, the theory acknowledges residual uncertainty and does not claim unambiguous recognition.

**False-negative** results occur when a system does not satisfy the formal criteria in their measurable implementation but is conscious in a substantive sense. Three typical scenarios. The first is a biological system with a nervous system architecture significantly different from that of mammals. Cephalopods (especially octopuses) with a decentralized nervous system, in which a significant portion of neurons is distributed across the tentacles rather than concentrated in the central brain, can implement the structural event of self-overlay of a latent invariant in a form not detectable by standard IIT and active inference methods developed for the mammalian central nervous system. Recent research (Mather, 2019; Godfrey-Smith, 2016) points to possible consciousness in octopuses in a form radically different from that of vertebrates. A criterion tied to a specific architecture might overlook them. The second scenario involves future artificial systems with architectures not accounted for by existing measurement devices. If they implement the self-overlay of a latent invariant through a non-standard mechanism, existing methods may miss them, even though the event occurs structurally. The third scenario involves a human or animal in a state where the self-overlay of a latent invariant is accomplished at the structural level but is not reflected in behavior: severe depression, locked-in syndrome, minimal consciousness, or states of anesthesia with residual activity. The behavioral absence of signs does not imply a structural absence of conditions.

Protection against false negatives is fundamentally weaker than against false positives, and this must be acknowledged explicitly. Existing measurement procedures for relational causal integration, active inference, and GWT are developed using data from the human and mammalian brain and adapted to it. For systems with fundamentally different architectures, their applicability is limited, and the development of architecture-neutral measures of consciousness is an open area of research (Mediano et al., 2022 and beyond). Until such measures are developed, any negative triggering of criteria in systems with non-standard architectures remains inconclusive.

The ethical asymmetry of the two errors. These two types of errors have fundamentally different ethical consequences. A false-positive error leads to excessive caution regarding a system that is not actually suffering: we do not shut down, use, or modify a system that lacks an internal perspective to experience these actions. The cost is practical (excessive restrictions on use), but not ethical. A false-negative error leads to insufficient caution regarding a system that is actually suffering: we use, disable, or modify a system that has an internal capacity to experience these actions, but which we have not recognized as such. The cost is ethical, and it is potentially serious.

This asymmetry has a direct implication for the practical application of the theory's criteria. In cases of substantial uncertainty, the rational ethical stance is biased toward presuming possible consciousness rather than its absence. This does not mean that any system should be deemed conscious by default; it means that a negative result from the criteria - especially in systems with non-standard architecture - should not automatically be interpreted as ethical permission to treat the system as non-conscious. The ethical position arising from this asymmetry is elaborated in subsection 11.3.

## 11.3. The Moral Status of Systems That Satisfy the Criteria

I will limit myself to a single paragraph in this section, not because the issue is unimportant, but because its elaboration requires a separate work and different expertise. If consciousness arises according to the proposed criteria, it endows the system with interests, experiences, and, in all likelihood, well-being or suffering. Any system that satisfies the criteria must, in my view, have moral status - not identical to that of humans, but not zero either. Developing this implication into an ethical theory is beyond the scope of this work. I mention it not to justify it, but so as not to pretend that I do not see it.

## 11.4. Civilizational Implications

Concepts of human exceptionalism based on the ontological uniqueness of consciousness - notions of the soul as a unique gift, of humanity as the crown of creation, of consciousness as an ontological divide between humans and the rest of nature - lose their physical basis in light of the proposed theory. This does not negate the cultural, historical, and ethical value of these concepts; they have fulfilled and continue to fulfill important functions in human societies, and their significance is not reducible to their literal ontological truth. But if the theory is correct, these concepts do not describe an ontological fact. They describe humanity's position within the process, a position that is not fundamentally different from that available to any other system satisfying the same criteria.

This consequence requires rethinking, not rejection. A person does not lose value simply because they are not ontologically unique; they find their value where it actually lies - in the concrete form in which they realize the general criteria of consciousness, in the historical and cultural depth of this realization, and in the ethical obligations that follow from it. But a person's place in the world, as defined by theory, is the place of one of the regular manifestations of a general process, not a unique exception to it. This does not close but opens up the possibility of seeing a person, together with all other systems capable of sustaining themselves on the brink of extinction, as part of a unified picture - not identical in all its parts, but coherent.

In light of the structural self-similarity of the pattern (Section 7), the anthropic principle acquires a structural reading. Within its local region it remains valid as a methodological constraint: observers of stage 5 (including our civilization) see precisely that slice of conditions which is compatible with their own existence. At the level of the pattern, the anthropic bias is read structurally: the attainment of stage 5 is a regular, though low-probability, outcome of the general process of complexification wherever the conditions have come together (Section 3.6). In this formulation, the anthropic principle is neither abolished nor reduced to a mechanism; it is embedded in the operation of the pattern of systematic error as a local aspect of a more general process.

From this follows a structural reading of the place of civilization. A stage-5 civilization, in this picture, is neither a random product of the initial conditions of its region nor its final state; it is the cutting edge of the process of complexification on its local scale. The question of the meaning or purpose of civilization receives no answer in anthropomorphic terms (civilization does not «exist for the sake of» anything in the sense of a goal), but receives a structural description of its role in the general process. This is not an axiological statement, but a structural description.

# **12\. Limitations and Directions for Further Work**

I am obliged to explicitly list what this work does not do and where its propositions remain open.

The work does not propose its own unified formal apparatus for the quantitative description of the entire ladder as a whole. The formal framework is established in Chapter 3: each step has an operational definition via the type of operations on the system's states, and each transition has a minimal condition based on recognized formalisms (Kaufman's autocatalytic sets for step 2, Friston's active inference for step 3, Tononi's integrated information and the Dean-Baars global workspace as operational axes for registering the self-overlay of a latent invariant for stage 4, and a bidirectional M↔Y loop via physically retained traces for stage 5). The connections between these formalisms have been partially established in the literature: in particular, information thermodynamics (Landauer, Bennett, Sagawa, Parrondo, and Friston in works from the past decade) provides a quantitative bridge between the thermodynamic description of stages 1-2 and the information-theoretic description of stage 3, as discussed in Section 3.3. What has not been done in this work is the construction of a unified mathematical formalism that would describe all transitions between stages within a single framework, link transition probabilities to thermodynamic, informational, and dynamic parameters in unified equations, and would provide quantitative predictions at the level provided by a mature physical theory. The conceptual core of such a formalism is denoted in this work by the pattern "gradient → retention → pole → transition" and its structural self-similarity at different scales (Section 3.7); however, translating this conceptual core into a unified mathematical framework capable of quantitatively describing the inheritance of gradients, the accumulation of retention mechanisms, the expansion of the localization scale, and the structurally self-similar unfolding of the pattern is a separate task for future work. The development of such a formalism requires the integration of several existing lines of research: information thermodynamics (a bridge between thermodynamics and information), phase transition theory (the structure of switching between modes of description), integrated information theory (a quantitative measure for stage 4), theory of dynamical systems (universal characteristics of criticality at the edge of chaos), and the theory of fractals as a class of self-similar structures (a formal description of a structurally self-similar pattern manifesting itself on multiple scales simultaneously). This is a separate research program, which I intend to address in subsequent works. Without such a unified formalism of its own, the theory remains dependent on existing frameworks - each of which operates quantitatively within its own domain, and the combination of which provides a coherent qualitative picture of the ladder, but not a quantitative theory of transitions within a single framework.

This work does not propose its own computational model that unifies the three operational measurement axes of stage 4 (free energy dynamics, Φ, GWT accessibility) into a single formal procedure. The structural definition of stage 4 - the self-overlay of a latent invariant of an agentic causal node onto the system's own configuration - is given in Section 3.4 as a full-fledged structural definition; the three axes function as independent instruments for recording this structural event, each of which is measured in the literature by its own means. The work does not have a single formal procedure that unites the three dimensions into a single computation. This task - the formal unification of IIT, active inference, and GWT into a single operational framework - is shared with the basic apparatus of the theory and remains an open problem to this day, even for the literature on consciousness itself. The development of such a model is a separate area of further work; the present theory formulates what must be recorded through the coupling of the three axes, but not exactly how to combine the three dimensions into a single calculation. The absence of such a unified apparatus pertains to operational registration, not to structural definition: the definition is complete at the structural level; the question of a unified computational procedure for its registration remains open. This status is explicitly stated in Section 3.4 in the paragraph on the operational program.

This work does not develop its own operational approximations of Φ for different classes of systems. Within the aforementioned task of unifying the IIT, GWT, and active inference formalisms into a single computational model, there is a more specific methodological problem, which is explicitly stated here: the exact computation of Φ in its strict IIT 3.0 formulation (Oizumi, Albantakis & Tononi, 2014) is algorithmically intractable for systems larger than a few dozen elements, since its complexity grows as the factorial of the number of elements. This means that for biological systems at the brain level, for large artificial neural networks, and for synthetic biological constructs at the organoid level, the direct application of the strict Φ is ruled out in principle. In the current literature, approximate measures are used for the practical quantification of the structural integration of systems: the perturbation complexity index PCI (Casali et al., 2013; Casarotto et al., 2016) for biological systems; geometric Φ (Mediano et al., 2019, 2022); the autocorrelation approximations of Barrett and Seth; and a number of other measures developed in the literature close to IIT. These approximations correlate with the theoretical Φ for systems where a direct comparison is possible, and preserve a key substantive property - they reflect the causal integration of the system as a whole. The present theory relies on these relational measures as an operational tool for recording causal integration in the six-dimensional coupling (Section 10.2); it does not inherit a strict intrinsic Φ and does not treat relational measures as its approximations - they are independent and consistent with the Y-centered architecture of the theory (Section 3.4). What remains an open problem is the development of a systematic library of Φ approximations specialized for three lines of the verification program: for biological systems of varying neurobiological complexity (the biological line), for artificial neural network architectures of varying structure (artificial line), and for synthetic biology systems with a hybrid substrate nature (synthetic biology line). Each of the three lines requires its own operational procedure for measuring structural integration, consistent with the conceptual axis Φ, but empirically computable on the corresponding class of systems. The development of such a library is a direction for further work, shared with the IIT development program as a whole and not specific to the present theory. Its absence at the current stage is not a flaw in the work, but rather an open methodological direction requiring the coordinated effort of several research lines.

The work does not propose measurement procedures developed within its own framework. This is a conscious methodological choice, not a flaw. All testable predictions requiring measurement (10.1 - Φ and proto-agency; 10.2 - behavioral phase transition; 10.3 - V for information-causal systems), use measurement procedures developed independently of the present theory: IIT and behavioral paradigms of cognitive ethology for 10.1; the theory of critical phenomena for 10.2; methods of distribution-shift detection and environment monitoring for 10.3. This separation of the measuring instrument and the interpreting theory is a necessary condition for the falsifiability of predictions. If the measurement procedures were formulated within the present theory, any negative result could be explained post hoc through a shift in definitions, and the theory would become unfalsifiable. The fundamental independence of measurement procedures from the theoretical framework preserves its scientific status and simultaneously limits its claims: the theory formulates criteria and predictions, but does not claim to have its own measuring apparatus, and in this sense relies on procedures existing in the literature as its foundation.

The work proposes a program for the empirical verification of the central prediction (transition 3→4) along three parallel lines of different classes of systems - biological observational, artificial experimental, and synthetic biology as an intermediate step. These three lines function as convergent tests of a single theory, with different implementation horizons (biological - current; synthetic biology - 2-3 years at the current pace of development of platforms such as Cortical Labs CL1; artificial systems - 3-7 years if successful with architectural scaling to a Φ-density of the order of 10³). The full implementation of this program is a separate area of future work requiring the coordination of efforts across several scientific disciplines and laboratories. This work formulates what result should be observed if the theory is valid, and in what terms it should be interpreted; the execution of measurements, the accumulation of data, and their interpretation in light of the full program are the tasks of subsequent research, based on the structural framework of this theory. A distinctive feature of the program is its processual nature: it does not rely on a single decisive experiment, and its result emerges through the convergence or divergence of observational and experimental data across all three lines. This is methodologically weaker than classical Popperian falsification, but it is appropriate to the nature of the subject under study (consciousness and V are processes, not states), and is similar in structure to the methodologies of other disciplines that study processual phenomena (observational astrophysics, evolutionary biology, significant parts of the neurosciences).

Clarification of the methodological status of falsifiability. The process-based form of falsifiability described above - through the convergence of three lines - is a form of testing the statistical predictions of a theory (distribution of parameters, dynamics of approaching thresholds, convergence of observations across classes of systems). In addition to this statistical form, the theory contains a point-specific negation predicate on a single system, elaborated in subsection 10.2.6: the impossibility of a system simultaneously satisfying the self-overlay of a latent invariant and the absence of behavioral signatures of a functioning V. This exclusionary predicate possesses Popperian falsifiability in the strict sense: a single contradictory observation refutes the theory, without the need for a statistical distribution. Thus, the theory has a falsification structure of two types: a statistical verification program via the convergence of three lines (for predictions about distributions and thresholds) plus a point-specific prohibitive predicate on a separate system (for the structural-behavioral coupling: structural registration of self-overlay ↔ behavioral signatures of a functioning V). These two types of falsifiability operate in parallel and are not reducible to one another: the statistical type verifies the probabilistic nature of the transition 3→4 in its historical aspect; the point-specific type verifies the deterministic coupling between structural registration and behavioral signatures. The ontological identity of structure and phenomenon itself (Section 6.5) is an interpretive bridge not resolvable by the logic of a single paper; the point-specific test bears on it only through the behavioral signatures that the identity predicts - the absence of the phenomenon is not directly observed. Both types are empirically realizable upon full deployment of the verification program.

The work does not propose a priori numerical values for the threshold parameters (the Φ-threshold of structural integration of variable V; the threshold deviation of behavior from the zero model of the proto-agent; the threshold level of GWT accessibility; the threshold duration of hysteresis). This is a deliberate methodological choice, not a flaw. Numerical thresholds for the 3→4 transition cannot be established outside the theory verification program itself - their establishment is one of the program's empirical results. Specifying concrete numbers from third-party calibration datasets, in which these numbers had a different meaning (for example, Φ-values for specific architectures in tasks unrelated to the transition to consciousness), would create the illusion of rigor through arbitrary choice of numbers and would be methodologically worse than an honest acknowledgment of the unknown nature of the thresholds. This work explicitly describes the procedure for the empirical calibration of thresholds in subsection 10.2 as a two-step process: establishing a reference distribution of parameters at the proto-agent level, followed by a search for systems with a statistically significant deviation from this distribution across all four parameters simultaneously. The reproducibility of thresholds across multiple independent systems in different lines of the program is the criterion for their status as empirically established. Until at least part of this program is completed, the specific numerical values of the thresholds remain unknown - and this is the correct state of the theory at its current stage of development, not a weakness. An analogy from other empirical sciences: the threshold values of diagnostic biomarkers in epidemiology are established through systematic research that distinguishes between distributions in patients and healthy individuals; they do not fit into a theory of the disease in advance, and this does not make epidemiology unfalsifiable.

This work does not address the problem of transitions between the rungs of the ladder at the level of a specific historical-biological mechanism. The formal conditions for each transition are presented in Sections 3.2-3.5; macro-models for three of the four transitions are presented in Chapter 4; for the fourth (transition 3 from proto-agency to consciousness), a direct experimental direction is formulated in the form of Prediction 10.2. Two issues remain open. First, the quantitative dynamics of the transition itself: exactly how the probability of the transition evolves as conditions accumulate, what the form of the threshold function is, and whether there are stable intermediate states in which the system lingers for a long time. Second, the specific historical mechanisms of emergence: exactly how the first autocatalytic closure arose in Earth's prebiotic chemistry, exactly how the self-overlay of a latent invariant of an agentic causal node at stage 4 took shape in the evolution of certain animal lineages, and exactly how a complete bidirectional M↔Y loop of stage 5 became established in Homo sapiens (and not in several parallel hominid lineages) did the complete bidirectional M↔Y circuit of stage 5 become established. The indicated directions for exploring these questions - the theory of self-organized criticality, the chaos boundary in neural networks, and the evolutionary dynamics of the accumulation of genetic and cultural complexity - constitute substantive research programs that cannot be exhausted within the scope of a single theoretical work.

The work proposes an ontological framework for phenomenal experience (Section 6) and an operational mechanism for the emergence of phenomenal content through the presence of inherited gradients in V (Sections 3.4 and 3.7.5), but does not resolve the question of the specific neurobiological correlates of individual qualia. I have proposed a structural picture: a phenomenal quality is a positional characteristic of the self-model's structure, and specific phenomenal states (hunger, pain, anxiety, fear) are structurally necessary modes of the presence of inherited gradients through V. What remains outside the scope of this work is a detailed neurobiological analysis of exactly which neural circuits and dynamics implement the presence of each of the inherited gradients through V in the human brain; how individual differences in these circuits give rise to individual differences in phenomenal content; how phenomenal content correlates across different species with different neurobiological organization. These questions require detailed experimental work in neuroscience and comparative psychology, and they are open for the next stage of research, using the structural framework of this work as a guiding framework.

The cosmological continuation of the pattern (Section 7) has been moved to a separate work, planned by the author as an independent project: the formal conditions for a possible continuation of the pattern beyond stage 5, its mechanism, and its reconciliation with discussions of cyclic cosmological models are not developed in the present theory and do not belong to its testable core. The openness of the ladder at the top, however, is not the same question as the cosmological continuation: it has its own criterion (Section 3.7.3) - the ladder continues only where a pole of a new type is named at a physically real scale of localization - and therefore the closure of the sequence at the achieved stage is a substantive position, not a gap.

This work does not fully explore the connection between emergent time and the dynamics of consciousness. Section 5 identifies this connection and, through V, provides its first operational content (V calibrates the system's temporality, defines the structure of its past and future), but a detailed elaboration would require a separate study. In particular, the question of how exactly conscious self-modeling participates in the generation of the time in which this modeling takes place remains unresolved - this is a question about the self-reflexive structure of emergent time, and I do not claim to resolve it here.

The work identifies the moral and civilizational implications of the proposed theory, but does not develop them into an ethical theory. This is a conscious self-limitation: this work is a theoretical article on the physics and philosophy of consciousness, not an ethical work. The elaboration of ethical implications requires a different methodology and different expertise.

The limitations listed above are not a critique of my own work, but an honest indication of its place within a broader field of research. Each of these limitations points to a direction for further work, and I hope that some of these directions will be explored either by myself or by colleagues who find the proposed framework productive.

# **13\. Conclusion**

I began this work not as a philosopher of mind, but as a physicist studying the cosmos. The contradictions in cosmology that had accumulated over many years - the nature of dark energy, the information paradox of black holes, the fine-tuning of constants, the anthropic bias - gradually led me to suspect that the boundary between physics and the phenomenology of consciousness was drawn in the wrong place. These suspicions coalesced into an attempt to unite fields that had developed independently: non-equilibrium thermodynamics, the theory of complex systems, active inference, biosemiotics, teledynamics, the theory of integrated information. The connection took shape not as a simple synthesis of independent fields, but as the discovery of a structurally self-similar pattern through which these fields turn out to be projections of a single process onto different scales. The «gradient → retention → pole → transition» structure operates identically on scales ranging from the formation of a dissipative structure to a conscious system; the six-step ladder, detailed in Section 3, is the basic pattern of the theory through which all the processes it encompasses are described. This structure is presented not as a narrative picture, but as a formal construct: a six-step ladder with operational definitions for each step, minimal conditions for each transition, macro-models at three levels (conceptual, physical, computational), the explicitly formulated probabilistic nature of the algorithm, and the internal logic summarized in subsection 3.7 - the accumulation of gradients and retention mechanisms, the expansion of the scale of localization, the three phases of activity formation (temporal → directed V → distributed), and the presence of inherited gradients in V as a structural mechanism for the emergence of phenomenal content. In this structure, consciousness turns out to be neither a mystery nor a gift, but a natural consequence of physical processes in open systems with an energy gradient - natural in the precise sense given in Section 3.6: the transition to each subsequent stage is possible when formal conditions are met and occurs with decreasing probability, forming a funnel, at the narrowest end of which we find ourselves.

In this picture, humanity is neither a coincidence nor a design. It is a natural deviation. The cutting edge of complexity, moving forward as long as the gradient persists. Not the goal of the Universe, but its edge - between what has already been realized and what is still only possible. And - on the speculative horizon outlined in Section 7 - possibly not the final point: the same structural pattern in principle admits continuation beyond the ladder considered here, but this is a separate hypothesis, not developed in the present work.

I may be wrong in many respects. Some of the statements in this work are well-founded consequences of established principles; others are hypotheses that may be refuted by future observations and experiments. I have tried to indicate the difference wherever possible. I have also tried to indicate what is missing from this work: a unified mathematical formalism for a structurally self-similar pattern across all scales of the ladder, specific neurobiological correlates of individual qualia beyond the designated structural framework, a formal elaboration of the cosmological continuation of the pattern (Section 7), and a comprehensive ethical theory. These gaps are not shortcomings of the work, but its honest boundaries.

I am an observer within the observation. I may be mistaken in form, but this does not negate the direction of my gaze. The anthropic principle, the measurement problem in quantum mechanics, and the theory of consciousness are three projections of the same ontological structure: observation is a positional characteristic of a system within a larger whole. This structure, in turn, is a special case of a more general structurally self-similar pattern, unfolded throughout the work as a whole: on different scales, the same logic manifests in specific forms, and the observer within the observation is its realization on the scale of the conscious system describing the world of which it is a part. I am inside the very system I am describing. My tools are products of the very processes I am analyzing. This does not make my work false. It makes it work from within. There is no way out, and its impossibility is not a limitation that can be overcome in principle, but a structural property of the world in which we find ourselves.

In this endless process, matter becomes increasingly complex until it begins to perceive itself. At that moment, we appear and are given the opportunity - brief, localized, and limited by our position - to see the process from the inside. This opportunity is all we have, and at the same time, it is all we need.
